	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Metallica</h1>
	
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
		<div id="contentSub"></div>
		
		
		
		<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>
		<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">This article is about the band. For its eponymous fifth album, see <a href="/wiki/Metallica_(album)" title="Metallica (album)">Metallica (album)</a>. For other uses, see <a href="/wiki/Metallica_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="Metallica (disambiguation)">Metallica (disambiguation)</a>.</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>
<div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">American heavy metal band</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>
<table class="infobox vcard plainlist" style="width:22em"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold;background-color: #b0c4de"><div style="display:inline;" class="fn org">Metallica</div></th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><a href="/wiki/File:Metallica_Live_at_The_O2,_London,_England,_22_October_2017.jpg" class="image" title="Members of Metallica onstage"><img alt="Members of Metallica onstage" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Metallica_Live_at_The_O2%2C_London%2C_England%2C_22_October_2017.jpg/267px-Metallica_Live_at_The_O2%2C_London%2C_England%2C_22_October_2017.jpg" decoding="async" width="267" height="200" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Metallica_Live_at_The_O2%2C_London%2C_England%2C_22_October_2017.jpg/400px-Metallica_Live_at_The_O2%2C_London%2C_England%2C_22_October_2017.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Metallica_Live_at_The_O2%2C_London%2C_England%2C_22_October_2017.jpg/533px-Metallica_Live_at_The_O2%2C_London%2C_England%2C_22_October_2017.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2008" data-file-height="1506" /></a><div>Metallica in <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>, England in 2017. <p><b>Metallica</b> is an American <a href="/wiki/Heavy_metal_music" title="Heavy metal music">heavy metal</a> band. The band was formed in 1981 in <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a> by vocalist/guitarist <a href="/wiki/James_Hetfield" title="James Hetfield">James Hetfield</a> and drummer <a href="/wiki/Lars_Ulrich" title="Lars Ulrich">Lars Ulrich</a>, and has been based in <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco" title="San Francisco">San Francisco</a> for most of its career.<sup id="cite_ref-SF_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SF-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MetallicaOfficial_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MetallicaOfficial-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> The group's fast tempos, instrumentals and aggressive musicianship made them one of the founding "big four" bands of <a href="/wiki/Thrash_metal" title="Thrash metal">thrash metal</a>, alongside <a href="/wiki/Megadeth" title="Megadeth">Megadeth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anthrax_(American_band)" title="Anthrax (American band)">Anthrax</a> and <a href="/wiki/Slayer" title="Slayer">Slayer</a>. Metallica's current lineup comprises founding members and primary songwriters Hetfield and Ulrich, longtime lead guitarist <a href="/wiki/Kirk_Hammett" title="Kirk Hammett">Kirk Hammett</a> and bassist <a href="/wiki/Robert_Trujillo" title="Robert Trujillo">Robert Trujillo</a>. Guitarist <a href="/wiki/Dave_Mustaine" title="Dave Mustaine">Dave Mustaine</a> (who went on to form Megadeth after being fired from the band) and bassists <a href="/wiki/Ron_McGovney" title="Ron McGovney">Ron McGovney</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cliff_Burton" title="Cliff Burton">Cliff Burton</a> (who died in a bus accident in Sweden in 1986) and <a href="/wiki/Jason_Newsted" title="Jason Newsted">Jason Newsted</a> are former members of the band.
</p><p>Metallica earned a growing fan base in the <a href="/wiki/Underground_music" title="Underground music">underground music</a> community and won critical acclaim with its first five albums.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> The band's third album, <i><a href="/wiki/Master_of_Puppets" title="Master of Puppets">Master of Puppets</a></i> (1986), was described as one of the heaviest and most influential thrash metal albums. Its <a href="/wiki/Eponym" title="Eponym">eponymous</a> fifth album, <i><a href="/wiki/Metallica_(album)" title="Metallica (album)">Metallica</a></i> (1991), the band's first to root predominantly in heavy metal, appealed to a more mainstream audience, achieving substantial commercial success and selling over 16 million copies in the United States to date, making it the best-selling album of the <a href="/wiki/Nielsen_SoundScan" title="Nielsen SoundScan">SoundScan</a> era. After experimenting with different genres and directions in subsequent releases, the band returned to its thrash metal roots with the release of its ninth album, <i><a href="/wiki/Death_Magnetic" title="Death Magnetic">Death Magnetic</a></i> (2008), which drew similar praise to that of the band's earlier albums.
</p><p>In 2000, Metallica <a href="/wiki/Metallica_v._Napster,_Inc." title="Metallica v. Napster, Inc.">led the case</a> against the <a href="/wiki/Peer-to-peer_file_sharing" title="Peer-to-peer file sharing">peer-to-peer file sharing</a> service <a href="/wiki/Napster" title="Napster">Napster</a>, in which the band and several other artists filed lawsuits against the service for sharing their copyright-protected material without consent; after reaching a settlement, Napster became a <a href="/wiki/Napster_(pay_service)" title="Napster (pay service)">pay-to-use service</a> in 2003. Metallica was the subject of the acclaimed 2004 <a href="/wiki/Documentary_film" title="Documentary film">documentary film</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Some_Kind_of_Monster_(film)" title="Some Kind of Monster (film)">Some Kind of Monster</a></i>, which documented the sometimes troubled production of the band's eighth album, <i><a href="/wiki/St._Anger" title="St. Anger">St. Anger</a></i> (2003), and the internal struggles within the band at the time. In 2009, Metallica was inducted into the <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame" title="Rock and Roll Hall of Fame">Rock and Roll Hall of Fame</a>. The band wrote the screenplay for and starred in the 2013 <a href="/wiki/IMAX" title="IMAX">IMAX</a> <a href="/wiki/Concert_film" title="Concert film">concert film</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Metallica:_Through_the_Never" title="Metallica: Through the Never">Metallica: Through the Never</a></i>, in which the band performed live against a fictional <a href="/wiki/Thriller_film" title="Thriller film">thriller</a> storyline.
</p><p>Metallica has released ten studio albums, four live albums, a cover album, five extended plays, 37 singles and 39 music videos. The band has won nine <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" title="Grammy Award">Grammy Awards</a> from 23 nominations, and its last six studio albums (beginning with <i>Metallica</i>) have consecutively debuted at number one on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a>. Metallica ranks as one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_best-selling_music_artists" title="List of best-selling music artists">most commercially successful bands of all time</a>, having sold over 125 million albums worldwide as of 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-sold_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sold-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> Metallica has been listed as one of the greatest artists of all time by magazines such as <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i>, which ranked them at no. 61 on its <a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone%27s_100_Greatest_Artists_of_All_Time" title="Rolling Stone&#39;s 100 Greatest Artists of All Time"><i>100 Greatest Artists of All Time</i></a> list.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> As of 2017, Metallica is the third best-selling music artist since Nielsen SoundScan began tracking sales in 1991,<sup id="cite_ref-Album_Sales_1_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Album_Sales_1-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> selling a total of 58 million albums in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-16"><a href="#Awards_and_nominations"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">Awards and nominations</span></a></li>
<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-17"><a href="#Discography"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Discography</span></a></li>
<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-18"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>
<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-19"><a href="#Notes"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Notes</span></a></li>
<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-20"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>
<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-21"><a href="#Sources"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">Sources</span></a></li>
<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-22"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>
</ul>
</div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>
<h3><span id="Formation_and_early_years_.281981.E2.80.931982.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Formation_and_early_years_(1981–1982)">Formation and early years (1981–1982)</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Metallica_wordmark.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Metallica_wordmark.svg/220px-Metallica_wordmark.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="92" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Metallica_wordmark.svg/330px-Metallica_wordmark.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Metallica_wordmark.svg/440px-Metallica_wordmark.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="558" data-file-height="234" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Metallica_wordmark.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The classic Metallica logo designed by James Hetfield, used on most of the band's releases.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>Metallica was formed in <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a> in late 1981 when Danish-born drummer <a href="/wiki/Lars_Ulrich" title="Lars Ulrich">Lars Ulrich</a> placed an advertisement in a Los Angeles newspaper, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Recycler" title="The Recycler">The Recycler</a></i>, which read, "Drummer looking for other metal musicians to jam with <a href="/wiki/Tygers_of_Pan_Tang" title="Tygers of Pan Tang">Tygers of Pan Tang</a>, <a href="/wiki/Diamond_Head_(English_band)" title="Diamond Head (English band)">Diamond Head</a> and <a href="/wiki/Iron_Maiden" title="Iron Maiden">Iron Maiden</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-Timeline_1_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Timeline_1-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> Guitarists <a href="/wiki/James_Hetfield" title="James Hetfield">James Hetfield</a> and Hugh Tanner of <a href="/wiki/Leather_Charm" title="Leather Charm">Leather Charm</a> answered the advertisement. Although he had not formed a band, Ulrich asked <a href="/wiki/Metal_Blade_Records" title="Metal Blade Records">Metal Blade Records</a> founder <a href="/wiki/Brian_Slagel" title="Brian Slagel">Brian Slagel</a> if he could record a song for the label's upcoming compilation album, <i><a href="/wiki/Metal_Massacre" title="Metal Massacre">Metal Massacre</a></i>. Slagel accepted, and Ulrich recruited Hetfield to sing and play rhythm guitar.<sup id="cite_ref-Timeline_1_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Timeline_1-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> The band was officially formed on October 28, 1981, five months after Ulrich and Hetfield first met.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r889293853/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{display:flex;flex-direction:row;clear:left;flex-wrap:wrap;width:100%;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{margin:1px;float:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .theader{clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;align-self:center;background-color:transparent;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{text-align:left;background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-left{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-right{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-center{text-align:center}@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;max-width:none!important;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{justify-content:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:214px;max-width:214px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:212px;max-width:212px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Metallica_Of_Wolf_and_Man_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Metallica_Of_Wolf_and_Man_%28cropped%29.jpg/210px-Metallica_Of_Wolf_and_Man_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="210" height="156" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Metallica_Of_Wolf_and_Man_%28cropped%29.jpg/315px-Metallica_Of_Wolf_and_Man_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Metallica_Of_Wolf_and_Man_%28cropped%29.jpg/420px-Metallica_Of_Wolf_and_Man_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1991" data-file-height="1483" /></a></div></div></div><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:212px;max-width:212px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Lars_Ulrich_(Metallica).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Lars_Ulrich_%28Metallica%29.jpg/210px-Lars_Ulrich_%28Metallica%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="210" height="156" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Lars_Ulrich_%28Metallica%29.jpg/315px-Lars_Ulrich_%28Metallica%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Lars_Ulrich_%28Metallica%29.jpg/420px-Lars_Ulrich_%28Metallica%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1725" data-file-height="1284" /></a></div></div></div><div class="trow"><div class="thumbcaption" style="text-align:left;background-color:transparent">Metallica founding members James Hetfield (top) and Lars Ulrich (bottom)</div></div></div></div>
<p>The band name came from Ulrich's friend Ron Quintana, who was brainstorming names for a fanzine and was considering <i>MetalMania</i> or <i>Metallica</i>. After hearing the two names, Ulrich wanted Metallica for his band, so he suggested Quintana use MetalMania instead.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Dave_Mustaine" title="Dave Mustaine">Dave Mustaine</a> replied to an advertisement for a lead guitarist; Ulrich and Hetfield recruited him after seeing his expensive guitar equipment. In early 1982, Metallica recorded its first original song, "Hit the Lights", for the <i>Metal Massacre I</i> compilation. Hetfield played bass, rhythm guitar and sang while Lloyd Grant was credited with a guitar solo and Lars Ulrich played drums.<sup id="cite_ref-Timeline_1_10-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Timeline_1-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> <i>Metal Massacre I</i> was released on June 14, 1982; early pressings listed the band incorrectly as "Mettallica", angering the band.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> The song generated <a href="/wiki/Word_of_mouth" title="Word of mouth">word of mouth</a> and the band played its first live performance on March 14, 1982, at Radio City in <a href="/wiki/Anaheim,_California" title="Anaheim, California">Anaheim, California</a>, with newly recruited bassist <a href="/wiki/Ron_McGovney" title="Ron McGovney">Ron McGovney</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Their first live success came early; they were chosen to open for British heavy metal band <a href="/wiki/Saxon_(band)" title="Saxon (band)">Saxon</a> at one gig of their 1982 US tour. This was Metallica's second gig. Metallica recorded its first demo, <i><a href="/wiki/Power_Metal_(Metallica_album)" class="mw-redirect" title="Power Metal (Metallica album)">Power Metal</a></i>, whose name was inspired by Quintana's early business cards in early 1982.
</p><p>The term "<a href="/wiki/Thrash_metal" title="Thrash metal">thrash metal</a>" was coined in February 1984 by <i><a href="/wiki/Kerrang!" title="Kerrang!">Kerrang!</a></i> journalist <a href="/wiki/Malcolm_Dome" title="Malcolm Dome">Malcolm Dome</a> in reference to <a href="/wiki/Anthrax_(American_band)" title="Anthrax (American band)">Anthrax</a>'s song "<a href="/wiki/Metal_Thrashing_Mad" class="mw-redirect" title="Metal Thrashing Mad">Metal Thrashing Mad</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> Prior to this, Hetfield referred to Metallica's sound as "<a href="/wiki/Power_metal" title="Power metal">power metal</a>". In late 1982, Ulrich and Hetfield attended a show at the <a href="/wiki/West_Hollywood" class="mw-redirect" title="West Hollywood">West Hollywood</a> nightclub <a href="/wiki/Whisky_a_Go_Go" title="Whisky a Go Go">Whisky a Go Go</a>, which featured bassist <a href="/wiki/Cliff_Burton" title="Cliff Burton">Cliff Burton</a> in the band <a href="/wiki/Trauma_(band)" title="Trauma (band)">Trauma</a>. The two were "blown away" by Burton's use of a <a href="/wiki/Wah-wah_pedal" title="Wah-wah pedal">wah-wah pedal</a> and asked him to join Metallica. Hetfield and Mustaine wanted McGovney to leave because they thought he "didn't contribute anything, he just followed".<sup id="cite_ref-Timeline_2_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Timeline_2-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> Although Burton initially declined the offer, by the end of the year, he had accepted on the condition the band move to <a href="/wiki/El_Cerrito,_California" title="El Cerrito, California">El Cerrito</a> in the <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Bay_Area" title="San Francisco Bay Area">San Francisco Bay Area</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Timeline_2_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Timeline_2-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> Metallica's first live performance with Burton was at the nightclub The Stone in March 1983, and the first recording to feature Burton was the <i>Megaforce</i> demo (1983).<sup id="cite_ref-Timeline_2_17-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Timeline_2-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Metallica was ready to record their debut album, but when Metal Blade was unable to cover the cost, they began looking for other options. Concert promoter <a href="/wiki/Johny_Zazula" class="mw-redirect" title="Johny Zazula">Johny "Z" Zazula</a>, who had heard the demo <i>No Life 'til Leather</i> (1982), offered to broker a record deal between Metallica and <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>-based record labels. After those record labels showed no interest, Zazula borrowed enough money to cover the recording budget and signed Metallica to his own label, <a href="/wiki/Megaforce_Records" title="Megaforce Records">Megaforce Records</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Pillsbury_2006_2_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pillsbury_2006_2-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Kill_.27Em_All_and_Ride_the_Lightning_.281983.E2.80.931985.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Kill_'Em_All_and_Ride_the_Lightning_(1983–1985)"><i>Kill 'Em All</i> and <i>Ride the Lightning</i> (1983–1985)</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Priest_feast_22_-_megadeth_05.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Priest_feast_22_-_megadeth_05.jpg/220px-Priest_feast_22_-_megadeth_05.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Priest_feast_22_-_megadeth_05.jpg/330px-Priest_feast_22_-_megadeth_05.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Priest_feast_22_-_megadeth_05.jpg/440px-Priest_feast_22_-_megadeth_05.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1134" data-file-height="759" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Priest_feast_22_-_megadeth_05.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Dave Mustaine went on to found rival band Megadeth after being fired from the band in 1983.</div></div></div>
<p>In May 1983, Metallica traveled to <a href="/wiki/Rochester,_New_York" title="Rochester, New York">Rochester, New York</a> to record its debut album, <i>Metal Up Your Ass</i>, which was produced by Paul Curcio.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> The other members decided to eject Mustaine from the band because of his drug and alcohol abuse, and violent behavior just before the recording sessions on April 11, 1983.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Exodus_(American_band)" title="Exodus (American band)">Exodus</a> guitarist <a href="/wiki/Kirk_Hammett" title="Kirk Hammett">Kirk Hammett</a> replaced Mustaine the same afternoon.<sup id="cite_ref-Pillsbury_2006_2_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pillsbury_2006_2-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> Metallica's first live performance with Hammett was on April 16, 1983, at a nightclub in <a href="/wiki/Dover,_New_Jersey" title="Dover, New Jersey">Dover, New Jersey</a> called The Showplace;<sup id="cite_ref-Timeline_2_17-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Timeline_2-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> the support act was Anthrax's original line-up, which included <a href="/wiki/Dan_Lilker" title="Dan Lilker">Dan Lilker</a> and <a href="/wiki/Neil_Turbin" title="Neil Turbin">Neil Turbin</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> This was the first time the two bands performed live together.<sup id="cite_ref-Timeline_2_17-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Timeline_2-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Mustaine, who went on to form <a href="/wiki/Megadeth" title="Megadeth">Megadeth</a>, has expressed his dislike for Hammett in interviews, saying Hammett "stole" his job.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> Mustaine was "pissed off" because he believes Hammett became popular by playing guitar leads that Mustaine himself had written.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> In a 1985 interview with <i><a href="/wiki/Metal_Forces" title="Metal Forces">Metal Forces</a></i>, Mustaine said, "it's real funny how Kirk Hammett ripped off every lead break I'd played on that <i>No Life 'til Leather</i> tape and got voted No.&#160;1 guitarist in your magazine".<sup id="cite_ref-Metal_Forces_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Metal_Forces-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> On Megadeth's debut album <i><a href="/wiki/Killing_Is_My_Business..._and_Business_Is_Good!" title="Killing Is My Business... and Business Is Good!">Killing Is My Business... and Business Is Good!</a></i> (1985), Mustaine included the song "Mechanix", which Metallica had previously reworked and retitled "The Four Horsemen" on <i>Kill 'Em All</i>. Mustaine said he did this to "straighten Metallica up" because Metallica referred to Mustaine as a drunk and said he could not play guitar.<sup id="cite_ref-Metal_Forces_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Metal_Forces-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:177px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kirk2010.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Kirk2010.jpg/175px-Kirk2010.jpg" decoding="async" width="175" height="264" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Kirk2010.jpg/263px-Kirk2010.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Kirk2010.jpg/350px-Kirk2010.jpg 2x" data-file-width="398" data-file-height="600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kirk2010.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Kirk Hammett replaced Mustaine in 1983, and has been with the band ever since.</div></div></div>
<p>Because of conflicts with its record label and the distributors' refusal to release an album titled <i>Metal Up Your Ass</i>, the album was renamed <i><a href="/wiki/Kill_%27Em_All" title="Kill &#39;Em All">Kill 'Em All</a></i>. It was released on Megaforce Records in the U.S. and on <a href="/wiki/Music_for_Nations" title="Music for Nations">Music for Nations</a> in Europe, and peaked at number 155 on the <i>Billboard</i> 200 in 1986.<sup id="cite_ref-Whitburn_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Whitburn-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference plainlinks nourlexpansion" id="ref_a"><a class="external autonumber" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Metallica#endnote_a">[1]</a></sup> Although the album was not initially a financial success, it earned Metallica a growing fan base in the underground metal scene.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> To support the release, Metallica embarked on the <a href="/wiki/Kill_%27Em_All_for_One" class="mw-redirect" title="Kill &#39;Em All for One">Kill 'Em All for One</a> tour with <a href="/wiki/Raven_(band)" class="mw-redirect" title="Raven (band)">Raven</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> In February 1984, Metallica supported <a href="/wiki/Venom_(band)" title="Venom (band)">Venom</a> on the Seven Dates of Hell tour, during which the bands performed in front of 7,000 people at the Aardschok Festival in <a href="/wiki/Zwolle" title="Zwolle">Zwolle</a>, Netherlands.<sup id="cite_ref-Timeline_3_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Timeline_3-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Metallica recorded its second studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Ride_the_Lightning" title="Ride the Lightning">Ride the Lightning</a></i>, at <a href="/wiki/Sweet_Silence_Studios" title="Sweet Silence Studios">Sweet Silence Studios</a> in <a href="/wiki/Copenhagen" title="Copenhagen">Copenhagen</a>, Denmark. It was released in August 1984 and reached number 100 on the <i>Billboard</i> 200.<sup id="cite_ref-Charts_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Charts-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> A French printing press mistakenly printed green covers for the album, which are now considered collectors' items. Mustaine received writing credit for "Ride the Lightning" and "The Call of Ktulu".<sup id="cite_ref-Timeline_3_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Timeline_3-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Elektra_Records" title="Elektra Records">Elektra Records</a> <a href="/wiki/A%26R" class="mw-redirect" title="A&amp;R">A&amp;R</a> director Michael Alago, and co-founder of Q-Prime Management Cliff Burnstein, attended a Metallica concert in September 1984. They were impressed with the performance, signed Metallica to Elektra, and made the band a client of Q-Prime Management.<sup id="cite_ref-Timeline_4_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Timeline_4-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> Metallica's growing success was such that the band's British label Music for Nations released "<a href="/wiki/Creeping_Death" title="Creeping Death">Creeping Death</a>" as a limited edition single, which sold 40,000 copies as an import in the U.S. Two of the three songs on the record—cover versions of Diamond Head's "<a href="/wiki/Am_I_Evil%3F" title="Am I Evil?">Am I Evil?</a>" and <a href="/wiki/Blitzkrieg_(band)" title="Blitzkrieg (band)">Blitzkrieg</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Buried_Alive_(Blitzkrieg_song)" title="Buried Alive (Blitzkrieg song)">Blitzkrieg</a>"—appeared on the 1988 Elektra reissue of <i>Kill 'Em All</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> Metallica embarked on its first major European tour with <a href="/wiki/Tank_(band)" title="Tank (band)">Tank</a> to an average crowd of 1,300. Returning to the U.S., it embarked upon a tour co-headlining with <a href="/wiki/W.A.S.P._(band)" title="W.A.S.P. (band)">W.A.S.P.</a> and supported by <a href="/wiki/Armored_Saint" title="Armored Saint">Armored Saint</a>. Metallica played its largest show at the <a href="/wiki/Monsters_of_Rock" title="Monsters of Rock">Monsters of Rock</a> festival at <a href="/wiki/Donington_Park#Music_festivals" title="Donington Park">Donington Park</a>, England, on August 17, 1985, with <a href="/wiki/Bon_Jovi" title="Bon Jovi">Bon Jovi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ratt" title="Ratt">Ratt</a>, playing to 70,000 people. At a show in <a href="/wiki/Oakland,_California" title="Oakland, California">Oakland, California</a>, at the <a href="/wiki/Day_on_the_Green" title="Day on the Green">Day on the Green</a> festival, the band played to a crowd of 60,000.<sup id="cite_ref-Timeline_4_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Timeline_4-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Master_of_Puppets_and_Burton.27s_death_.281986.E2.80.931987.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Master_of_Puppets_and_Burton's_death_(1986–1987)"><i>Master of Puppets</i> and Burton's death (1986–1987)</span></h3>
<p>Metallica's third studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Master_of_Puppets" title="Master of Puppets">Master of Puppets</a></i>, was recorded at <a href="/wiki/Sweet_Silence_Studios" title="Sweet Silence Studios">Sweet Silence Studios</a> and was released in March 1986. The album reached number 29 on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a> and spent 72 weeks on the chart.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> It was the band's first album to be certified <a href="/wiki/Music_recording_sales_certification#RIAA_certification" class="mw-redirect" title="Music recording sales certification">gold</a> on November 4, 1986, and was certified six times platinum in 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> Steve Huey of <a href="/wiki/AllMusic" title="AllMusic">AllMusic</a> considered the album "the band's greatest achievement".<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> Following the release of the album, Metallica supported <a href="/wiki/Ozzy_Osbourne" title="Ozzy Osbourne">Ozzy Osbourne</a> on a U.S. tour.<sup id="cite_ref-Timeline_4_30-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Timeline_4-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> Hetfield broke his wrist while skateboarding; he continued with the tour, performing vocals, with guitar technician <a href="/wiki/John_Marshall_(guitarist)" title="John Marshall (guitarist)">John Marshall</a> playing rhythm guitar.<sup id="cite_ref-Timeline_5_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Timeline_5-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On September 27, 1986, during the European leg of Metallica's <a href="/wiki/Damage,_Inc._Tour" title="Damage, Inc. Tour">Damage, Inc. Tour</a>, members drew cards to determine which bunks on the tour bus they would sleep in. Burton won and chose to sleep in Hammett's bunk. At around sunrise near <a href="/wiki/D%C3%B6rarp" title="Dörarp">Dörarp</a>, Sweden, the bus driver lost control and skidded, which caused the bus to overturn several times. Ulrich, Hammett, and Hetfield sustained no serious injuries; however, bassist Burton was pinned under the bus and died. Hetfield said:
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:177px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Jason_Curtis_Newsted.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Jason_Curtis_Newsted.jpg/175px-Jason_Curtis_Newsted.jpg" decoding="async" width="175" height="266" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Jason_Curtis_Newsted.jpg/263px-Jason_Curtis_Newsted.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Jason_Curtis_Newsted.jpg/350px-Jason_Curtis_Newsted.jpg 2x" data-file-width="823" data-file-height="1250" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Jason_Curtis_Newsted.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Jason Newsted joined Metallica soon after Cliff Burton's death in 1986.</div></div></div>
<blockquote><p>I saw the bus lying right on him. I saw his legs sticking out. I freaked. The bus driver, I recall, was trying to yank the blanket out from under him to use for other people. I just went, 'Don't fucking do that!' I already wanted to kill the [bus driver]. I don't know if he was drunk or if he hit some ice. All I knew was, he was driving and Cliff wasn't alive anymore.<sup id="cite_ref-Timeline_5_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Timeline_5-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<p>Burton's death left Metallica's future in doubt. The three remaining members decided Burton would want them to carry on, and with the Burton family's blessings the band sought a replacement.<sup id="cite_ref-Timeline_6_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Timeline_6-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> Roughly 40 people, including Hammett's childhood friend, <a href="/wiki/Les_Claypool" title="Les Claypool">Les Claypool</a> of <a href="/wiki/Primus_(band)" title="Primus (band)">Primus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Troy_Gregory" title="Troy Gregory">Troy Gregory</a> of <a href="/wiki/Prong_(band)" title="Prong (band)">Prong</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Jason_Newsted" title="Jason Newsted">Jason Newsted</a>, formerly of <a href="/wiki/Flotsam_and_Jetsam_(band)" title="Flotsam and Jetsam (band)">Flotsam and Jetsam</a>, auditioned for the band. Newsted learned Metallica's entire set list; after the audition Metallica invited him to Tommy's Joynt in San Francisco. Hetfield, Ulrich, and Hammett decided on Newsted as Burton's replacement; Newsted's first live performance with Metallica was at the Country Club in <a href="/wiki/Reseda,_California" class="mw-redirect" title="Reseda, California">Reseda, California</a>. The members initiated Newsted by tricking him into eating a ball of <a href="/wiki/Wasabi" title="Wasabi">wasabi</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Timeline_6_36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Timeline_6-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After Newsted joined Metallica, the band left its El Cerrito practice space—a suburban house formerly rented by sound engineer <a href="/wiki/Mark_Whitaker_(music_producer)" class="mw-redirect" title="Mark Whitaker (music producer)">Mark Whitaker</a> dubbed "the Metalli-mansion"—and relocated to the adjacent cities of <a href="/wiki/Berkeley,_California" title="Berkeley, California">Berkeley</a> and <a href="/wiki/Albany,_California" title="Albany, California">Albany</a> before eventually settling in the Marin County city of <a href="/wiki/San_Rafael,_California" title="San Rafael, California">San Rafael</a>, north of San Francisco.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Metallica finished its tour in the early months of 1987. In March 1987, Hetfield again broke his wrist while skateboarding, forcing the band to cancel an appearance on <i><a href="/wiki/Saturday_Night_Live" title="Saturday Night Live">Saturday Night Live</a></i>. In August 1987, an all-covers <a href="/wiki/Extended_play" title="Extended play">extended play</a> (EP) titled <i><a href="/wiki/The_$5.98_E.P.:_Garage_Days_Re-Revisited" title="The $5.98 E.P.: Garage Days Re-Revisited">The $5.98 E.P.: Garage Days Re-Revisited</a></i> was released. The EP was recorded in an effort to use the band's newly constructed recording studio, test Newsted's talents, and to relieve grief and stress following the death of Burton. A video titled <i><a href="/wiki/Cliff_%27Em_All" title="Cliff &#39;Em All">Cliff 'Em All</a></i> commemorating Burton's three years in Metallica was released in 1987; the video included bass solos, home videos, and pictures.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="...And_Justice_for_All_and_Metallica_.281988.E2.80.931993.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="...And_Justice_for_All_and_Metallica_(1988–1993)"><i>...And Justice for All</i> and <i>Metallica</i> (1988–1993)</span></h3>
<p>Metallica's first studio album since Burton's death, <i><a href="/wiki/...And_Justice_for_All_(album)" title="...And Justice for All (album)">...And Justice for All</a></i>, was released in 1988. The album was a commercial success, reaching number six on the <i>Billboard</i> 200, and was the band's first album to enter the top 10.<sup id="cite_ref-Charts_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Charts-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> The album was certified platinum nine weeks after its release.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> There were complaints about the production; Steve Huey of AllMusic said Ulrich's drums were clicking more than thudding, and the guitars "buzz thinly".<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> To promote the album, Metallica embarked on a tour called <a href="/wiki/Damaged_Justice" title="Damaged Justice">Damaged Justice</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Metallica_Damaged_Justice_Tour.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Metallica_Damaged_Justice_Tour.jpg/220px-Metallica_Damaged_Justice_Tour.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Metallica_Damaged_Justice_Tour.jpg/330px-Metallica_Damaged_Justice_Tour.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/d6/Metallica_Damaged_Justice_Tour.jpg 2x" data-file-width="429" data-file-height="282" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Metallica_Damaged_Justice_Tour.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Metallica performing during its Damaged Justice Tour in 1988</div></div></div>
<p>In 1989, Metallica received its first <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" title="Grammy Award">Grammy Award</a> nomination for <i>...And Justice for All</i> in the new <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Hard_Rock/Metal_Performance_Vocal_or_Instrumental" title="Grammy Award for Best Hard Rock/Metal Performance Vocal or Instrumental">Best Hard Rock/Metal Performance Vocal or Instrument</a> category. Metallica was the favorite to win but the award was given to <a href="/wiki/Jethro_Tull_(band)" title="Jethro Tull (band)">Jethro Tull</a> for the album <i><a href="/wiki/Crest_of_a_Knave" title="Crest of a Knave">Crest of a Knave</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Rockin&#39;_on_an_Island_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rockin&#39;_on_an_Island-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> The award was controversial with fans and the press; Metallica was standing off-stage waiting to receive the award after performing the song "<a href="/wiki/One_(Metallica_song)" title="One (Metallica song)">One</a>". Jethro Tull had been advised by its manager not to attend the ceremony because he was expecting Metallica to win.<sup id="cite_ref-Rockin&#39;_on_an_Island_43-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rockin&#39;_on_an_Island-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> The award was named in <i><a href="/wiki/Entertainment_Weekly" title="Entertainment Weekly">Entertainment Weekly</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;s</span> "Grammy's 10 Biggest Upsets".<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Following the release of <i>...And Justice for All</i>, Metallica released its debut music video for the song "One", which the band performed in an abandoned warehouse. The footage was remixed with the film <i><a href="/wiki/Johnny_Got_His_Gun_(film)" title="Johnny Got His Gun (film)">Johnny Got His Gun</a></i>. Rather than organize an ongoing licensing deal, Metallica purchased the rights to the film. The remixed video was submitted to MTV with an alternative, performance-only version that was held back in case MTV banned the remixed version. MTV accepted the remixed version; the video was viewers' first exposure to Metallica. In 1999, it was voted number 38 in MTV's "Top 100 Videos of All Time" countdown;<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> it was featured in the network's 25th Anniversary edition of <i>ADD Video</i>, which showcased the most popular videos on MTV in the last 25 years.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In October 1990, Metallica entered <a href="/wiki/17_Hertz_Studio" title="17 Hertz Studio">One on One Recording's</a> studio in North Hollywood to record its next album. <a href="/wiki/Bob_Rock" title="Bob Rock">Bob Rock</a>, who had worked with <a href="/wiki/Aerosmith" title="Aerosmith">Aerosmith</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Cult" title="The Cult">The Cult</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bon_Jovi" title="Bon Jovi">Bon Jovi</a>, and <a href="/wiki/M%C3%B6tley_Cr%C3%BCe" title="Mötley Crüe">Mötley Crüe</a>, was hired as the producer. <i><a href="/wiki/Metallica_(album)" title="Metallica (album)">Metallica</a></i>—also known as <i>The Black Album</i>—was remixed three times, cost <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$1 million</span>, and ended three marriages.<sup id="cite_ref-Timeline_8_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Timeline_8-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> Although the release was delayed until 1991, <i>Metallica</i> debuted at number one in ten countries, selling 650,000 units in the U.S. during its first week.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> The album brought Metallica mainstream attention; it has been certified 16 times platinum in the U.S., which makes it the 25th-best-selling album in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-Top_100_Albums_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Top_100_Albums-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> The making of <i>Metallica</i> and the following tour was documented in <i><a href="/wiki/A_Year_and_a_Half_in_the_Life_of_Metallica" title="A Year and a Half in the Life of Metallica">A Year and a Half in the Life of Metallica</a></i>. The tour in support of the album, called the <a href="/wiki/Wherever_We_May_Roam_Tour" title="Wherever We May Roam Tour">Wherever We May Roam Tour</a>, lasted 14 months and included dates in the U.S., Japan, and the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-Timeline_8_47-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Timeline_8-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> In April 1992, Metallica appeared at <a href="/wiki/The_Freddie_Mercury_Tribute_Concert" title="The Freddie Mercury Tribute Concert">The Freddie Mercury Tribute Concert</a> and performed a three-song set.<sup id="cite_ref-Purvis_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Purvis-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> Hetfield later performed "<a href="/wiki/Stone_Cold_Crazy" title="Stone Cold Crazy">Stone Cold Crazy</a>" with the remaining members of <a href="/wiki/Queen_(band)" title="Queen (band)">Queen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tony_Iommi" title="Tony Iommi">Tony Iommi</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Purvis_50-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Purvis-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On August 8, 1992, during the co-headlining <a href="/wiki/Guns_N%27_Roses/Metallica_Stadium_Tour" title="Guns N&#39; Roses/Metallica Stadium Tour">Guns N' Roses/Metallica Stadium Tour</a>, Hetfield suffered second and <a href="/wiki/Third_degree_burns" class="mw-redirect" title="Third degree burns">third degree burns</a> to his arms, face, hands, and legs. There had been some confusion with the new pyrotechnics setup, which resulted in Hetfield walking into a 12-foot (3.7&#160;m) flame during "Fade to Black". Newsted said Hetfield's skin was "bubbling like on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Toxic_Avenger_(film)" title="The Toxic Avenger (film)">The Toxic Avenger</a></i>".<sup id="cite_ref-Timeline_9_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Timeline_9-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>  Metallica returned to the stage 17 days later with guitar technician and <a href="/wiki/Metal_Church" title="Metal Church">Metal Church</a> member John Marshall replacing Hetfield on guitar for the remainder of the tour, although Hetfield was able to sing. Later in 1993, Metallica went on the <a href="/wiki/Nowhere_Else_to_Roam" title="Nowhere Else to Roam">Nowhere Else to Roam Tour</a>, playing five shows in <a href="/wiki/Mexico_City" title="Mexico City">Mexico City</a>. <i><a href="/wiki/Live_Shit:_Binge_%26_Purge" title="Live Shit: Binge &amp; Purge">Live Shit: Binge &amp; Purge</a></i>, the band's first box set, was released in November 1993. The collection contained three live CDs, three home videos, and a book filled with riders and letters.<sup id="cite_ref-Timeline_9_51-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Timeline_9-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Load.2C_Reload.2C_Garage_Inc._and_S.26M_.281994.E2.80.931999.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Load,_Reload,_Garage_Inc._and_S&amp;M_(1994–1999)"><i>Load</i>, <i>Reload</i>, <i>Garage Inc.</i> and <i>S&amp;M</i> (1994–1999)</span></h3>
<p>After almost three years of touring to promote <i>Metallica</i>, including a headlining performance at <a href="/wiki/Woodstock_%2794" title="Woodstock &#39;94">Woodstock '94</a>, Metallica returned to the studio to write and record its sixth studio album. The band went on a brief hiatus in the summer of 1995 and played a short tour, Escape from the Studio '95, comprising three outdoor shows, including a headline show at <a href="/wiki/Donington_Park" title="Donington Park">Donington Park</a> supported by <a href="/wiki/Slayer" title="Slayer">Slayer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Skid_Row_(American_band)" title="Skid Row (American band)">Skid Row</a>, <a href="/wiki/Slash%27s_Snakepit" title="Slash&#39;s Snakepit">Slash's Snakepit</a>, <a href="/wiki/Therapy%3F" title="Therapy?">Therapy?</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Corrosion_of_Conformity" title="Corrosion of Conformity">Corrosion of Conformity</a>. The band spent about a year writing and recording new songs, resulting in the release of <i><a href="/wiki/Load_(album)" title="Load (album)">Load</a></i> in 1996. <i>Load</i> debuted at number one on the <i>Billboard</i> 200 and <a href="/wiki/ARIA_Charts" title="ARIA Charts">ARIA Charts</a>; it was the band's second number-one album.<sup id="cite_ref-Charts_29-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Charts-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> The cover art, <i>Blood and Semen III</i>, was created by <a href="/wiki/Andres_Serrano" title="Andres Serrano">Andres Serrano</a>, who pressed a mixture of his own semen and blood between sheets of plexiglass.<sup id="cite_ref-Timeline_10_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Timeline_10-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> The release marked a change in the band's musical direction and a new image; the bandmembers' hair was cut. Metallica headlined the alternative rock festival <a href="/wiki/Lollapalooza" title="Lollapalooza">Lollapalooza</a> festival in mid-1996.<sup id="cite_ref-Playboy_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Playboy-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Load_review_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Load_review-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:James_Hetfield_-_Cardiff_1996.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/James_Hetfield_-_Cardiff_1996.jpg/220px-James_Hetfield_-_Cardiff_1996.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="129" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/James_Hetfield_-_Cardiff_1996.jpg/330px-James_Hetfield_-_Cardiff_1996.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/James_Hetfield_-_Cardiff_1996.jpg/440px-James_Hetfield_-_Cardiff_1996.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1954" data-file-height="1148" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:James_Hetfield_-_Cardiff_1996.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>James Hetfield performing with the band during its tour for <i>Load</i> in 1996</div></div></div>
<p>During early production of the album, the band had recorded enough material to fill a double album. It was decided that half of the songs were to be released; the band would continue to work on the remaining songs and release them the following year. This resulted in follow-up album titled <i><a href="/wiki/Reload_(Metallica_album)" title="Reload (Metallica album)">Reload</a></i>. The cover art was again created by Serrano, this time using a mixture of blood and urine.<sup id="cite_ref-Timeline_10_52-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Timeline_10-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> <i>Reload</i> debuted at number one on the <i>Billboard</i> 200 and reached number two on the Top Canadian Album chart.<sup id="cite_ref-Charts_29-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Charts-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> Hetfield said in the 2004 documentary film <i><a href="/wiki/Some_Kind_of_Monster_(film)" title="Some Kind of Monster (film)">Some Kind of Monster</a></i> that the band initially thought some of the songs on these albums were of average quality; these were "polished and reworked" until judged releasable.<sup id="cite_ref-Some_Kind_of_Monster_film_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Some_Kind_of_Monster_film-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> To promote <i>Reload</i>, Metallica performed "<a href="/wiki/Fuel_(song)" title="Fuel (song)">Fuel</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/The_Memory_Remains" title="The Memory Remains">The Memory Remains</a>" with <a href="/wiki/Marianne_Faithfull" title="Marianne Faithfull">Marianne Faithfull</a> on <a href="/wiki/NBC" title="NBC">NBC</a>'s <i>Saturday Night Live</i> in December 1997.<sup id="cite_ref-Timeline_11_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Timeline_11-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1998, Metallica compiled a double album of cover songs, <i><a href="/wiki/Garage_Inc." title="Garage Inc.">Garage Inc.</a></i> The first disc contained newly recorded covers of songs by <a href="/wiki/Diamond_Head_(English_band)" title="Diamond Head (English band)">Diamond Head</a>, <a href="/wiki/Killing_Joke" title="Killing Joke">Killing Joke</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Misfits_(band)" title="Misfits (band)">Misfits</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thin_Lizzy" title="Thin Lizzy">Thin Lizzy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mercyful_Fate" title="Mercyful Fate">Mercyful Fate</a>, <a href="/wiki/Black_Sabbath" title="Black Sabbath">Black Sabbath</a>, and others. The second disc featured the original version of <i>The $5.98 E.P.: Garage Days Re-Revisited</i>, which had become a scarce collectors' item. The album entered the <i>Billboard</i> 200 at number two.<sup id="cite_ref-Timeline_11_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Timeline_11-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On April 21 and 22, 1999, Metallica recorded two performances with the <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Symphony" title="San Francisco Symphony">San Francisco Symphony</a> conducted by <a href="/wiki/Michael_Kamen" title="Michael Kamen">Michael Kamen</a>, who had previously worked with producer Rock on "<a href="/wiki/Nothing_Else_Matters" title="Nothing Else Matters">Nothing Else Matters</a>". Kamen approached Metallica in 1991 with the idea of pairing the band's music with a symphony orchestra. Kamen and his staff of over 100 composed additional orchestral material for Metallica songs. Metallica wrote two new Kamen-scored songs for the event, "<a href="/wiki/No_Leaf_Clover" title="No Leaf Clover">No Leaf Clover</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/S%26M_(Metallica_album)" class="mw-redirect" title="S&amp;M (Metallica album)">-Human</a>". The audio recording and concert footage were released in 1999 as the album and concert film <i><a href="/wiki/S%26M_(album)" title="S&amp;M (album)">S&amp;M</a></i>. It entered the <i>Billboard</i> 200 at number two and the Australian ARIA charts and Top Internet Albums chart at number one.<sup id="cite_ref-Charts_29-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Charts-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Napster_controversy.2C_Newsted.27s_departure_and_Some_Kind_of_Monster_.282000.E2.80.932002.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Napster_controversy,_Newsted's_departure_and_Some_Kind_of_Monster_(2000–2002)">Napster controversy, Newsted's departure and <i>Some Kind of Monster</i> (2000–2002)</span></h3>
<p>In 2000, Metallica discovered that a demo of its song "<a href="/wiki/I_Disappear" title="I Disappear">I Disappear</a>", which was supposed to be released in combination with the <a href="/wiki/Mission:_Impossible_II_(soundtrack)" class="mw-redirect" title="Mission: Impossible II (soundtrack)"><i>Mission: Impossible II</i> soundtrack</a>, was receiving radio airplay. Tracing the source of the leak, the band found the file on the <a href="/wiki/Napster" title="Napster">Napster</a> <a href="/wiki/Peer-to-peer" title="Peer-to-peer">peer-to-peer</a> file-sharing network, and also found that the band's entire catalogue was freely available.<sup id="cite_ref-Testimony_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Testimony-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Metallica_v._Napster,_Inc." title="Metallica v. Napster, Inc.">Legal action was initiated</a> against Napster; Metallica filed a lawsuit at the <a href="/wiki/U.S._District_Court" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. District Court">U.S. District Court</a>, <a href="/wiki/Central_District_of_California" class="mw-redirect" title="Central District of California">Central District of California</a>, alleging that Napster violated three areas of the law: <a href="/wiki/Copyright_infringement" title="Copyright infringement">copyright infringement</a>, unlawful use of digital audio interface device, and the <a href="/wiki/Racketeer_Influenced_and_Corrupt_Organizations_Act" title="Racketeer Influenced and Corrupt Organizations Act">Racketeer Influenced and Corrupt Organizations Act</a> (RICO).<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:177px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lars_Ulrich_The_Rock_Copenhagen.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Lars_Ulrich_The_Rock_Copenhagen.JPG/175px-Lars_Ulrich_The_Rock_Copenhagen.JPG" decoding="async" width="175" height="222" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Lars_Ulrich_The_Rock_Copenhagen.JPG/263px-Lars_Ulrich_The_Rock_Copenhagen.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Lars_Ulrich_The_Rock_Copenhagen.JPG/350px-Lars_Ulrich_The_Rock_Copenhagen.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2118" data-file-height="2685" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lars_Ulrich_The_Rock_Copenhagen.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Lars Ulrich led the case against Napster for Metallica.</div></div></div>
<p>Ulrich provided a statement to the <a href="/wiki/Senate_Judiciary_Committee" class="mw-redirect" title="Senate Judiciary Committee">Senate Judiciary Committee</a> regarding copyright infringement on July 11, 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-Testimony_58-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Testimony-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Federal_Judge" class="mw-redirect" title="Federal Judge">Federal Judge</a> <a href="/wiki/Marilyn_Hall_Patel" title="Marilyn Hall Patel">Marilyn Hall Patel</a> ordered the site to place a <a href="/wiki/Content-control_software" title="Content-control software">filter</a> on the program within 72 hours or be shut down.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> A settlement between Metallica and Napster was reached when German media conglomerate <a href="/wiki/Bertelsmann" title="Bertelsmann">Bertelsmann</a> BMG showed interest in purchasing the rights to Napster for $94&#160;million. Under the terms of settlement, Napster agreed to block users who shared music by artists who do not want their music shared.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> On June 3, 2002, Napster filed for <a href="/wiki/Chapter_11" class="mw-redirect" title="Chapter 11">Chapter 11</a> protection under U.S. bankruptcy laws. On September 3, 2002, an American bankruptcy judge blocked the sale of Napster to Bertelsmann and forced Napster to liquidate its assets according to <a href="/wiki/Chapter_7,_Title_11,_United_States_Code" title="Chapter 7, Title 11, United States Code">Chapter 7</a> of the U.S. bankruptcy laws.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>At the <a href="/wiki/2000_MTV_Video_Music_Awards" title="2000 MTV Video Music Awards">2000 MTV Video Music Awards</a>, Ulrich appeared with host <a href="/wiki/Marlon_Wayans" title="Marlon Wayans">Marlon Wayans</a> in a skit that criticized the idea of using Napster to share music. Marlon played a college student listening to Metallica's "I Disappear". Ulrich walked in and asked for an explanation. Ulrich responded to Wayans' excuse that using Napster was just "sharing" by saying that Wayans' idea of sharing was "borrowing things that were not yours without asking". He called in the Metallica road crew, who proceeded to confiscate all of Wayans' belongings, leaving him almost naked in an empty room. Napster creator <a href="/wiki/Shawn_Fanning" title="Shawn Fanning">Shawn Fanning</a> responded later in the ceremony by presenting an award wearing a Metallica shirt, saying, "I borrowed this shirt from a friend. Maybe, if I like it, I'll buy one of my own." Ulrich was later booed on stage at the award show when he introduced the final musical act, <a href="/wiki/Blink-182" title="Blink-182">Blink-182</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:JunoAwards2009-BobRock_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/JunoAwards2009-BobRock_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-JunoAwards2009-BobRock_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/JunoAwards2009-BobRock_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-JunoAwards2009-BobRock_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/JunoAwards2009-BobRock_%28cropped%29.jpg/440px-JunoAwards2009-BobRock_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1660" data-file-height="1245" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:JunoAwards2009-BobRock_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Longtime producer Bob Rock recorded bass for <i>St. Anger</i> following Newsted's departure in 2001.</div></div></div>
<p>Newsted left Metallica on January 17, 2001, as plans were being made to enter the recording studio. He said he left the band for "private and personal reasons, and the physical damage I have done to myself over the years while playing the music that I love".<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> During a <i><a href="/wiki/Playboy" title="Playboy">Playboy</a></i> interview with Metallica, Newsted said he wanted to release an album with his <a href="/wiki/Side_project" title="Side project">side project</a>, <a href="/wiki/Echobrain" title="Echobrain">Echobrain</a>. Hetfield was opposed to the idea and said, "When someone does a side project, it takes away from the strength of Metallica", and that a side project is "like cheating on your wife in a way".<sup id="cite_ref-Playboy_53-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Playboy-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> Newsted said Hetfield had recorded vocals for a song used in the film <i><a href="/wiki/South_Park:_Bigger,_Longer_%26_Uncut" title="South Park: Bigger, Longer &amp; Uncut">South Park: Bigger, Longer &amp; Uncut</a></i>, and appeared on two Corrosion of Conformity albums. Hetfield replied, "My name isn't on those records. And I'm not out trying to sell them", and raised questions such as, "Where would it end? Does he start touring with it? Does he sell shirts? Is it his band?"<sup id="cite_ref-Playboy_53-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Playboy-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In April 2001, filmmakers <a href="/wiki/Joe_Berlinger" title="Joe Berlinger">Joe Berlinger</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Sinofsky" title="Bruce Sinofsky">Bruce Sinofsky</a> began following Metallica to document the recording process of the band's next studio album. Over two years they recorded more than 1,000 hours of footage. On July 19, 2001, before preparations to enter the recording studio, Hetfield entered <a href="/wiki/Drug_rehabilitation" title="Drug rehabilitation">rehab</a> to treat his "alcoholism and other addictions". All recording plans were put on hold and the band's future was in doubt.<sup id="cite_ref-Timeline_12_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Timeline_12-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> Hetfield left rehab on December 4, 2001,<sup id="cite_ref-Timeline_12_66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Timeline_12-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> and the band returned to the recording studio on April 12, 2002. Hetfield was required to limit his work to four hours a day between noon and 4&#160;pm, and to spend the rest of his time with his family.<sup id="cite_ref-Some_Kind_of_Monster_film_55-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Some_Kind_of_Monster_film-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> The footage recorded by Berlinger and Sinofsky was compiled into the documentary <i><a href="/wiki/Some_Kind_of_Monster_(film)" title="Some Kind of Monster (film)">Some Kind of Monster</a></i>, which premiered at the <a href="/wiki/Sundance_Film_Festival" title="Sundance Film Festival">Sundance Film Festival</a> in January 2004. In the documentary, Newsted said his former bandmates' decision to hire a therapist to help solve their problems which he felt they could have solved on their own was "really fucking lame and weak".<sup id="cite_ref-Some_Kind_of_Monster_film_55-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Some_Kind_of_Monster_film-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="St._Anger_and_Death_Magnetic_.282003.E2.80.932008.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="St._Anger_and_Death_Magnetic_(2003–2008)"><i>St. Anger</i> and <i>Death Magnetic</i> (2003–2008)</span></h3>
<p>In June 2003, Metallica's eighth studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/St._Anger" title="St. Anger">St. Anger</a></i>, debuted at number one on the <i>Billboard</i> 200, and drew mixed reactions from critics. Ulrich's "steely" sounding snare drum and the absence of guitar solos received particular criticism.<sup id="cite_ref-Metacritic_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Metacritic-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> Kevin Forest Moreau of <i>Shakingthrough.net</i> said, "the guitars stumble in a monotone of mid-level, processed rattle; the drums don't propel as much as struggle to disguise an all-too-turgid pace; and the rage is both unfocused and leavened with too much narcissistic navel-gazing".<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> Brent DiCrescenzo of <i><a href="/wiki/Pitchfork_(website)" title="Pitchfork (website)">Pitchfork</a></i> described it as "an utter mess".<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> However, <i><a href="/wiki/Blender_(magazine)" title="Blender (magazine)">Blender</a></i> magazine called it the "grimiest and grimmest of the band's Bob Rock productions", and <i><a href="/wiki/New_York_Magazine" class="mw-redirect" title="New York Magazine">New York Magazine</a></i> called it "utterly raw and rocking".<sup id="cite_ref-St_Anger_by_Metallica_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-St_Anger_by_Metallica-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> The title track, "<a href="/wiki/St._Anger_(song)" title="St. Anger (song)">St. Anger</a>", won the <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Metal_Performance" title="Grammy Award for Best Metal Performance">Grammy Award for Best Metal Performance</a> in 2004; it was used as the official theme song for <a href="/wiki/WWE" title="WWE">WWE</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/SummerSlam_(2003)" title="SummerSlam (2003)">SummerSlam 2003</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:177px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Robert_Trujillo_live_in_London_2008-09-15.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Robert_Trujillo_live_in_London_2008-09-15.jpg/175px-Robert_Trujillo_live_in_London_2008-09-15.jpg" decoding="async" width="175" height="218" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Robert_Trujillo_live_in_London_2008-09-15.jpg/263px-Robert_Trujillo_live_in_London_2008-09-15.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Robert_Trujillo_live_in_London_2008-09-15.jpg/350px-Robert_Trujillo_live_in_London_2008-09-15.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1459" data-file-height="1817" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Robert_Trujillo_live_in_London_2008-09-15.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Robert Trujillo joined Metallica in 2003 during the recording of <i>St. Anger</i>.</div></div></div>
<p>For the duration of <i>St. Anger</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s recording period, producer Bob Rock played bass on the album and in several live shows at which Metallica performed during that time.<sup id="cite_ref-Some_Kind_of_Monster_film_55-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Some_Kind_of_Monster_film-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> Once the record was completed, the band started to hold auditions for Newsted's permanent replacement. Bassists <a href="/wiki/Pepper_Keenan" title="Pepper Keenan">Pepper Keenan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jeordie_White" class="mw-redirect" title="Jeordie White">Jeordie White</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scott_Reeder_(bassist)" title="Scott Reeder (bassist)">Scott Reeder</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eric_Avery" title="Eric Avery">Eric Avery</a>, <a href="/wiki/Danny_Lohner" title="Danny Lohner">Danny Lohner</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Chris_Wyse" title="Chris Wyse">Chris Wyse</a>—among others—auditioned for the role. After three months of auditions, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Trujillo" title="Robert Trujillo">Robert Trujillo</a>, formerly of <a href="/wiki/Suicidal_Tendencies" title="Suicidal Tendencies">Suicidal Tendencies</a> and Ozzy Osbourne's band, was chosen as the new bassist.<sup id="cite_ref-Some_Kind_of_Monster_film_55-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Some_Kind_of_Monster_film-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> Newsted, who had joined Canadian thrash metal band <a href="/wiki/Voivod_(band)" title="Voivod (band)">Voivod</a> by that time, was Trujillo's replacement in Osbourne's band during the 2003 <a href="/wiki/Ozzfest" title="Ozzfest">Ozzfest</a> tour, which included Voivod.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Before the band's set at the 2004 <a href="/wiki/Download_Festival" title="Download Festival">Download Festival</a>, Ulrich was rushed to the hospital after having an anxiety seizure and was unable to perform.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> Hetfield searched for last-minute volunteers to replace Ulrich. Slayer drummer <a href="/wiki/Dave_Lombardo" title="Dave Lombardo">Dave Lombardo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Slipknot_(band)" title="Slipknot (band)">Slipknot</a> drummer <a href="/wiki/Joey_Jordison" title="Joey Jordison">Joey Jordison</a> volunteered. Lombardo performed "Battery" and "The Four Horsemen", Ulrich's drum technician Flemming Larsen performed "Fade to Black", and Jordison performed the remainder of the set.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> Having toured for two years in support of <i>St. Anger</i> on the Summer Sanitarium Tour 2003 and the <a href="/wiki/Madly_in_Anger_with_the_World_Tour" title="Madly in Anger with the World Tour">Madly in Anger with the World Tour</a>, with multi-platinum rock band <a href="/wiki/Godsmack" title="Godsmack">Godsmack</a> in support, Metallica took a break from performing and spent most of 2005 with friends and family. The band opened for <a href="/wiki/The_Rolling_Stones" title="The Rolling Stones">The Rolling Stones</a> at <a href="/wiki/AT%26T_Park" class="mw-redirect" title="AT&amp;T Park">SBC Park</a> in San Francisco on November 13 and 15, 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In December 2006, Metallica released a DVD titled <i><a href="/wiki/The_Videos_1989%E2%80%932004" title="The Videos 1989–2004">The Videos 1989–2004</a></i>, which sold 28,000 copies in its first week and entered the <i>Billboard</i> Top Videos chart at number three.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> Metallica recorded a guitar-based interpretation of <a href="/wiki/Ennio_Morricone" title="Ennio Morricone">Ennio Morricone</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/The_Ecstasy_of_Gold" title="The Ecstasy of Gold">The Ecstasy of Gold</a>" for a tribute album titled <i><a href="/wiki/We_All_Love_Ennio_Morricone" title="We All Love Ennio Morricone">We All Love Ennio Morricone</a></i>, which was released in February 2007. The track received a Grammy nomination at the <a href="/wiki/50th_Grammy_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="50th Grammy Awards">50th Grammy Awards</a> for the category "<a href="/wiki/Best_Rock_Instrumental_Performance" class="mw-redirect" title="Best Rock Instrumental Performance">Best Rock Instrumental Performance</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> A recording of "The Ecstasy of Gold" has been played to introduce Metallica's performances since the 1980s.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> Earlier that year, Metallica announced on its official website that after 15 years, long-time producer Bob Rock would not be producing the band's next studio album. Instead, the band chose to work with producer <a href="/wiki/Rick_Rubin" title="Rick Rubin">Rick Rubin</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> Metallica scheduled the release of <i><a href="/wiki/Death_Magnetic" title="Death Magnetic">Death Magnetic</a></i> as September 12, 2008, and the band filmed a music video for the album's first single, "<a href="/wiki/The_Day_That_Never_Comes" title="The Day That Never Comes">The Day That Never Comes</a>".
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Metallica_London_2008-09-15_Kirk_and_James.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Metallica_London_2008-09-15_Kirk_and_James.jpg/220px-Metallica_London_2008-09-15_Kirk_and_James.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="163" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Metallica_London_2008-09-15_Kirk_and_James.jpg/330px-Metallica_London_2008-09-15_Kirk_and_James.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Metallica_London_2008-09-15_Kirk_and_James.jpg/440px-Metallica_London_2008-09-15_Kirk_and_James.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2085" data-file-height="1545" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Metallica_London_2008-09-15_Kirk_and_James.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Metallica performing in London in 2008</div></div></div>
<p>On September 2, 2008, a record store in France began selling copies of <i>Death Magnetic</i> nearly two weeks before its scheduled worldwide release date,<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> which resulted in the album being made available on peer-to-peer clients. This prompted the band's UK distributor <a href="/wiki/Vertigo_Records" title="Vertigo Records">Vertigo Records</a> to officially release the album on September 10, 2008. Rumors of Metallica or Warner Bros. taking legal action against the French retailer were unconfirmed, though drummer Lars Ulrich responded to the <a href="/wiki/Internet_leak" title="Internet leak">leak</a> by saying, "...We're ten days from release. I mean, from here, we're golden. If this thing leaks all over the world today or tomorrow, happy days. Happy days. Trust me",<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> and, "By 2008 standards, that's a victory. If you'd told me six months ago that our record wouldn't leak until 10 days out, I would have signed up for that."<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><i>Death Magnetic</i> debuted at number one in the U.S. selling 490,000 units; Metallica became the first band to have five consecutive studio albums debut at number one in the history of the <i>Billboard</i> 200.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> A week after its release, <i>Death Magnetic</i> remained at number one on the <i>Billboard</i> 200 and the European album chart; it also became the fastest selling album of 2008 in Australia.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> <i>Death Magnetic</i> remained at number one on the <i>Billboard</i> 200 album chart for three consecutive weeks. Metallica was one of two artists whose album—the other being <a href="/wiki/Jack_Johnson_(musician)" title="Jack Johnson (musician)">Jack Johnson</a>'s album <i><a href="/wiki/Sleep_Through_the_Static" title="Sleep Through the Static">Sleep Through the Static</a></i>—remained on the <i>Billboard</i> 200 for three consecutive weeks at number one in 2008. <i>Death Magnetic</i> also remained at number one on <i>Billboard'</i>s Hard Rock, Modern Rock/Alternative and Rock album charts for five consecutive weeks. The album reached number one in 32 countries outside the U.S., including the UK, Canada, and Australia.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> In November 2008, Metallica's record deal with Warner Bros. ended and the band considered releasing its next album through the internet.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame_induction.2C_Lulu_and_Beyond_Magnetic_.282009.E2.80.932011.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame_induction,_Lulu_and_Beyond_Magnetic_(2009–2011)">Rock and Roll Hall of Fame induction, <i>Lulu</i> and <i>Beyond Magnetic</i> (2009–2011)</span></h3>
<p>On January 14, 2009, it was announced that Metallica would be inducted into the <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame" title="Rock and Roll Hall of Fame">Rock and Roll Hall of Fame</a> on April 4, 2009,<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> and that former bassist Jason Newsted—who left the band in 2001—would perform with the band at the ceremony.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> Initially, it was announced that the matter had been discussed and that bassist Trujillo had agreed not to play because he "wanted to see the Black Album band".<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> However, during the band's set of "Master of Puppets" and "Enter Sandman", both Trujillo and Newsted were on stage.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> Ray Burton, father of the late Cliff Burton, accepted the honor on his behalf. Although he was not to be inducted with them, Metallica invited Dave Mustaine to take part in the induction ceremony. Mustaine declined because of his touring commitments in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Metallica_at_the_O2_Arena,_March_28th_2009.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Metallica_at_the_O2_Arena%2C_March_28th_2009.jpg/220px-Metallica_at_the_O2_Arena%2C_March_28th_2009.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Metallica_at_the_O2_Arena%2C_March_28th_2009.jpg/330px-Metallica_at_the_O2_Arena%2C_March_28th_2009.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Metallica_at_the_O2_Arena%2C_March_28th_2009.jpg/440px-Metallica_at_the_O2_Arena%2C_March_28th_2009.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2873" data-file-height="1906" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Metallica_at_the_O2_Arena,_March_28th_2009.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Metallica performing in London in 2009</div></div></div>
<p>Metallica, Slayer, Megadeth, and Anthrax performed on the same bill for the first time on June 16, 2010, at <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Babice_Airport" title="Warsaw Babice Airport">Warsaw Babice Airport</a>, <a href="/wiki/Warsaw" title="Warsaw">Warsaw</a>, as a part of the <a href="/wiki/Sonisphere_Festival" title="Sonisphere Festival">Sonisphere Festival</a> series.
