The show in Sofia, Bulgaria, on June 22, 2010, was broadcast via satellite to cinemas.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> The bands also played concerts in <a href="/wiki/Bucharest" title="Bucharest">Bucharest</a> on June 26, 2010, and <a href="/wiki/Istanbul" title="Istanbul">Istanbul</a> on June 27, 2010. On June 28, 2010, <i>Death Magnetic</i> was certified double platinum by the <a href="/wiki/RIAA" class="mw-redirect" title="RIAA">RIAA</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> Metallica's <a href="/wiki/World_Magnetic_Tour" title="World Magnetic Tour">World Magnetic Tour</a> ended in <a href="/wiki/Melbourne" title="Melbourne">Melbourne</a> on November 21, 2010. The band had been touring for over two years in support of <i>Death Magnetic</i>. To accompany the final tour dates in Australia and New Zealand, a live, limited edition EP of past performances in Australia called <i><a href="/wiki/Six_Feet_Down_Under" title="Six Feet Down Under">Six Feet Down Under</a></i> was released.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> The EP was followed by <i><a href="/wiki/Six_Feet_Down_Under_(Part_II)" class="mw-redirect" title="Six Feet Down Under (Part II)">Six Feet Down Under (Part II)</a></i>, which was released on November 12, 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> Part 2 contains a further eight songs recorded during the first two Oceanic Legs of the World Magnetic Tour. On November 26, 2010, Metallica released a live EP titled <i><a href="/wiki/Live_at_Grimey%27s" title="Live at Grimey&#39;s">Live at Grimey's</a></i>, which was recorded in June 2008 at Grimey's Record Store, just before the band's appearance at <a href="/wiki/Bonnaroo_Music_Festival" title="Bonnaroo Music Festival">Bonnaroo Music Festival</a> that year.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In a June 2009 interview with Italy's Rock TV, Ulrich said Metallica was planning to continue touring until August 2010, and that there were no plans for a tenth album. He said he was sure the band would collaborate with producer Rick Rubin again.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/Blabbermouth.net" title="Blabbermouth.net">Blabbermouth.net</a>, the band was considering recording its next album in the second half of 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> In November 2010, during an interview with The Pulse of Radio, Ulrich said Metallica would return to writing in 2011. Ulrich said, "There's a bunch of balls in the air for 2011, but I think the main one is we really want to get back to writing again. We haven't really written since, what, '06, '07, and we want to get back to kind of just being creative again. Right now we are going to just chill out and then probably start up again in, I'd say, March or April, and start probably putting the creative cap back on and start writing some songs."<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Metallica3425.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Metallica3425.jpg/220px-Metallica3425.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Metallica3425.jpg/330px-Metallica3425.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Metallica3425.jpg/440px-Metallica3425.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2388" data-file-height="1791" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Metallica3425.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Metallica performing in Sacramento in 2009</div></div></div>
<p>In an interview at the April 2011 Big Four concert, Robert Trujillo said Metallica will work with Rick Rubin again as producer for the new album and were "really excited to write some new music. There's no shortage of riffage in Metallica world right now." He added, "The first album with Rick was also the first album for me, so in a lot of ways, you're kind of testing the water. Now that we're comfortable with Rick and his incredible engineer, Greg Fidelman, who worked with Slayer, actually, on this last record—it's my hero—it's a great team. And it's only gonna better; I really believe that. So I'm super-excited."<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> In June 2011, Rubin said Metallica had begun writing its new album.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>  On November 9, 2010, Metallica announced it would be headlining the <a href="/wiki/Rock_in_Rio" title="Rock in Rio">Rock in Rio</a> festival in <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro" title="Rio de Janeiro">Rio de Janeiro</a> on September 25, 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On December 13, 2010, the band announced it would again play as part of the "big four" during the Sonisphere Festival at <a href="/wiki/Knebworth_House" title="Knebworth House">Knebworth House</a>, Hertfordshire, on July 8, 2011. It was the first time all of the "big four" members played on the same stage in the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> On December 17, 2010, Another "big four" Sonisphere performance that would take place in France on July 9 was announced.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> On January 25, 2011, another "big four" performance on April 23, 2011, at the Empire Polo Club in <a href="/wiki/Indio,_California" title="Indio, California">Indio, California</a>, was announced. It was the first time all of the "big four" members played on the same stage in the U.S.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> On February 17, 2011, a show in <a href="/wiki/Gelsenkirchen" title="Gelsenkirchen">Gelsenkirchen</a>, Germany, on July 2, 2011, was announced.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> On February 22, a "big four" show in <a href="/wiki/Milan" title="Milan">Milan</a> on July 6, 2011, was announced.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> On March 2, 2011, another "big four" concert, which took place in <a href="/wiki/Gothenburg" title="Gothenburg">Gothenburg</a> on July 3, 2011, was announced.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> The final "big four" concert was in New York City, at Yankee Stadium, on September 14, 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On June 15, 2011, Metallica announced that recording sessions with singer-songwriter <a href="/wiki/Lou_Reed" title="Lou Reed">Lou Reed</a> had concluded. The album, which was titled <i><a href="/wiki/Lulu_(Lou_Reed_and_Metallica_album)" title="Lulu (Lou Reed and Metallica album)">Lulu</a></i>, was recorded over several months and comprised ten songs<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> based on <a href="/wiki/Frank_Wedekind" title="Frank Wedekind">Frank Wedekind</a>'s "Lulu" plays <i><a href="/wiki/Earth_Spirit_(play)" title="Earth Spirit (play)">Earth Spirit</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Pandora%27s_Box_(play)" title="Pandora&#39;s Box (play)">Pandora's Box</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-exclaim_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-exclaim-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> The album was released on October 31, 2011. The recording of the album was problematic at times; Lars Ulrich later said Lou Reed challenged him to a "street fight".<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> On October 16, 2011, Robert Trujillo confirmed that the band was back in the studio and writing new material. He said, "The writing process for the new Metallica album has begun. We've been in the studio with Rick Rubin, working on a couple of things, and we're going to be recording during the most of next year."<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Metallica_(6350334052).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Metallica_%286350334052%29.jpg/220px-Metallica_%286350334052%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="129" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Metallica_%286350334052%29.jpg/330px-Metallica_%286350334052%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Metallica_%286350334052%29.jpg/440px-Metallica_%286350334052%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3539" data-file-height="2069" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Metallica_(6350334052).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Metallica performing in Bangalore in 2011</div></div></div>
<p>Metallica was due to make its first appearance in India at the "India Rocks" concert, supporting the <a href="/wiki/2011_Indian_Grand_Prix" title="2011 Indian Grand Prix">2011 Indian Grand Prix</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> However, the concert was canceled when the venue was proven to be unsafe.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> Fans raided the stage during the event and the organizers were later arrested for fraud.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> Metallica made its Indian debut in Bangalore on October 30, 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> On November 10, it was announced that Metallica would headline the main stage on Saturday June 9, 2012, at the Download Festival at Donington Park and that the band would play <i>The Black Album</i> in its entirety.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> Metallica celebrated its 30th anniversary by playing four shows at the Fillmore in San Francisco in December 2011. The shows were exclusive to Met Club members and tickets were charged at $6 each or $19.81 for all four nights. The shows consisted of songs from the band's career and featured guest appearances by artists who had either helped or had influenced Metallica. These shows were notable because Lloyd Grant, Dave Mustaine, Jason Newsted, <a href="/wiki/Glenn_Danzig" title="Glenn Danzig">Glenn Danzig</a>, Ozzy Osbourne, <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Cantrell" title="Jerry Cantrell">Jerry Cantrell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Apocalyptica" title="Apocalyptica">Apocalyptica</a>, members of Diamond Head, and <a href="/wiki/King_Diamond" title="King Diamond">King Diamond</a> joined Metallica on stage for all appropriate songs.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> In December 2011, Metallica began releasing songs that were written for <i>Death Magnetic</i> but were not included on the album online.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> On December 13, 2011, the band released <i><a href="/wiki/Beyond_Magnetic" title="Beyond Magnetic">Beyond Magnetic</a></i>, a digital EP release exclusively on <a href="/wiki/ITunes" title="ITunes">iTunes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> It was released on CD in January 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Metallica:_Through_the_Never_and_Hardwired..._to_Self-Destruct_.282012.E2.80.932018.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Metallica:_Through_the_Never_and_Hardwired..._to_Self-Destruct_(2012–2018)"><i>Metallica: Through the Never</i> and <i>Hardwired... to Self-Destruct</i> (2012–2018)</span></h3>
<p>On February 7, 2012, Metallica announced that it would start a new music festival called <a href="/wiki/Orion_Music_%2B_More" title="Orion Music + More">Orion Music + More</a>, which took place on June 23 and 24, 2012, in Atlantic City. Metallica also confirmed that it would headline the festival on both days and would perform two of its most critically acclaimed albums in their entirety: <i>The Black Album</i> on one night, and <i>Ride the Lightning</i> on the other.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> In a July 2012 interview with Canadian radio station <a href="/wiki/CFOX-FM" title="CFOX-FM">99.3 The Fox</a>, Ulrich said Metallica would not release its new album until at least early 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-newalbum_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newalbum-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> In November 2012, Metallica left Warner Bros. Records and launched an independent record label, Blackened Recordings, which will produce the band's future releases.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> The band has acquired the rights to all of its studio albums, which will be reissued through the new label. Blackened releases will be licensed through Warner subsidiary <a href="/wiki/Rhino_Entertainment" title="Rhino Entertainment">Rhino Entertainment</a> in North America and internationally through <a href="/wiki/Universal_Music" class="mw-redirect" title="Universal Music">Universal Music</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-LATimes_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LATimes-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> On September 20, 2012, Metallica announced via its official website that a new DVD containing footage of shows it performed in Quebec in 2009 would be released that December; fans would get the chance to vote for two setlists that would appear on the DVD.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> The film, titled <i><a href="/wiki/Quebec_Magnetic" title="Quebec Magnetic">Quebec Magnetic</a></i>, was released in the U.S. on December 10, 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Metallica_2013.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Metallica_2013.jpg/220px-Metallica_2013.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Metallica_2013.jpg/330px-Metallica_2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Metallica_2013.jpg/440px-Metallica_2013.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4752" data-file-height="3168" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Metallica_2013.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Metallica at the <a href="/wiki/San_Diego_Comic-Con_International" class="mw-redirect" title="San Diego Comic-Con International">San Diego Comic-Con International</a> in 2013</div></div></div>
<p>In an interview with <i><a href="/wiki/Classic_Rock_(magazine)" title="Classic Rock (magazine)">Classic Rock</a></i> on January 8, 2013, Ulrich said regarding the band's upcoming album, "What we're doing now certainly sounds like a continuation [of <i>Death Magnetic</i>]". He also said, "I love Rick [Rubin]. We all love Rick. We're in touch with Rick constantly. We'll see where it goes. It would stun me if the record came out in 2013."<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> Also in 2013, the band starred in a 3D concert film titled <i><a href="/wiki/Metallica:_Through_the_Never" title="Metallica: Through the Never">Metallica: Through the Never</a></i>, which was directed by <a href="/wiki/Antal_Nimr%C3%B3d" class="mw-redirect" title="Antal Nimród">Antal Nimród</a> and was released in <a href="/wiki/IMAX" title="IMAX">IMAX</a> theaters on September 27.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> In an interview dated July 22, 2013, Ulrich told <i>Ultimate Guitar</i>, "2014 will be all about making a new Metallica record"; he said the album will most likely be released during 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> Kirk Hammett and Robert Trujillo later confirmed the band's intention to enter the studio.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> At the second Orion Music + More festival held in Detroit, the band played under the name "Dehaan"—a reference to actor <a href="/wiki/Dane_DeHaan" title="Dane DeHaan">Dane DeHaan</a>, who starred in <i>Metallica: Through the Never</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> The band performed its debut album <i>Kill 'Em All</i> in its entirety, celebrating the 30th anniversary of its release.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> On December 8, 2013, the band played a show called "Freeze 'Em All" in Antarctica, becoming the first band to play on all seven continents.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> The performance was filmed and released as a live album the same month.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>At the <a href="/wiki/56th_Annual_Grammy_Awards" title="56th Annual Grammy Awards">56th Annual Grammy Awards</a> in January 2014, Metallica performed "One" with Chinese pianist <a href="/wiki/Lang_Lang" title="Lang Lang">Lang Lang</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> In March 2014, Metallica began a tour called "Metallica By Request", in which fans request songs for the band to perform.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> A new song, titled "Lords of Summer" was written for the concerts and released as a "first take" demo in June 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> In June 2014, the band headlined the <a href="/wiki/Glastonbury_Festival" title="Glastonbury Festival">Glastonbury Festival</a> in an attempt to attract new fans. Ulrich said, "We have one shot, you never know if you'll be invited back".<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> In November 2014, Metallica performed at the closing ceremony of <a href="/wiki/BlizzCon" title="BlizzCon">BlizzCon 2014</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> In January 2015, Metallica announced a "Metallica Night" with the <a href="/wiki/San_Jose_Sharks" title="San Jose Sharks">San Jose Sharks</a>, which featured a Q&amp;A session with the band and a charity auction benefiting the San Francisco Bay Chapter of the Sierra Club, but no performances.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> They were announced to headline Lollapalooza in March 2015, returning to perform there for the first time in 20 years.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> On May 2, 2015, Metallica performed their third annual Metallica Day at <a href="/wiki/AT%26T_Park" class="mw-redirect" title="AT&amp;T Park">AT&amp;T Park</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> Metallica were also announced to play at <a href="/wiki/X_Games" title="X Games">X Games</a> for the first time at <a href="/wiki/X_Games_Austin_2015" title="X Games Austin 2015">X Games Austin 2015</a> in Austin, Texas.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> On June 14, 2015, Hetfield and Hammett performed <a href="/wiki/The_Star-Spangled_Banner" title="The Star-Spangled Banner">The Star-Spangled Banner</a> live via electric guitars prior to game 5 of the <a href="/wiki/2015_NBA_Finals" title="2015 NBA Finals">NBA Finals</a> between the <a href="/wiki/2014%E2%80%9315_Cleveland_Cavaliers_season" title="2014–15 Cleveland Cavaliers season">Cleveland Cavaliers</a> and <a href="/wiki/2014%E2%80%9315_Golden_State_Warriors_season" title="2014–15 Golden State Warriors season">Golden State Warriors</a> at <a href="/wiki/Oracle_Arena" title="Oracle Arena">Oracle Arena</a> in <a href="/wiki/Oakland,_California" title="Oakland, California">Oakland, California</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> In late October, the band unveiled a new website with an introduction from Ulrich containing footage from the studio of the band working on new material.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> On November 2, Metallica were announced to play "The Night Before" <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_50" title="Super Bowl 50">Super Bowl 50</a> at AT&amp;T Park.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> Metallica announced they would be opening the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Bank_Stadium" title="U.S. Bank Stadium">U.S. Bank Stadium</a> on August 20, 2016, with <a href="/wiki/Avenged_Sevenfold" title="Avenged Sevenfold">Avenged Sevenfold</a> and <a href="/wiki/Volbeat" title="Volbeat">Volbeat</a> as support.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Metallica_-_The_O2_-_Tuesday_24th_October_2017_MetallicaO2241017-3_(37955387006)_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Metallica_-_The_O2_-_Tuesday_24th_October_2017_MetallicaO2241017-3_%2837955387006%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-Metallica_-_The_O2_-_Tuesday_24th_October_2017_MetallicaO2241017-3_%2837955387006%29_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="153" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Metallica_-_The_O2_-_Tuesday_24th_October_2017_MetallicaO2241017-3_%2837955387006%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-Metallica_-_The_O2_-_Tuesday_24th_October_2017_MetallicaO2241017-3_%2837955387006%29_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Metallica_-_The_O2_-_Tuesday_24th_October_2017_MetallicaO2241017-3_%2837955387006%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/440px-Metallica_-_The_O2_-_Tuesday_24th_October_2017_MetallicaO2241017-3_%2837955387006%29_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3474" data-file-height="2417" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Metallica_-_The_O2_-_Tuesday_24th_October_2017_MetallicaO2241017-3_(37955387006)_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Metallica performing in London in 2017</div></div></div>
<p>In April 2016, during the week leading up to <a href="/wiki/Record_Store_Day" title="Record Store Day">Record Store Day</a>, for which the band was its ambassador for 2016, Ulrich told <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)">Billboard</a></i> that the band's expanded role within the music industry had played a part in the amount of time that it had taken to write and record the album. "The way we do things now is very different than the way we did things back in the days of <i>Kill 'Em All</i> and <i>Ride the Lightning</i>. Nowadays we like to do so many different things." Ulrich was also optimistic that production of the album had almost reached its completion. "Unless something radical happens it would be difficult for me to believe that it won't come out in 2016".<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> On August 18, 2016, the band announced via their website that their tenth studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Hardwired..._to_Self-Destruct" title="Hardwired... to Self-Destruct">Hardwired... to Self-Destruct</a></i>, would be released worldwide on November 18, 2016, via their independent label, Blackened Recordings. They also unveiled the track listing, album artwork, and released a music video for the album's first single, "Hardwired".<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup>  The album was released as scheduled<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> and debuted at number one on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Billboard_200_debut_162-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard_200_debut-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Metallica announced they would be touring the US in summer of 2017 for the <a href="/wiki/WorldWired_Tour" title="WorldWired Tour">WorldWired Tour</a>. The stadium tour also includes Avenged Sevenfold, Volbeat and <a href="/wiki/Gojira_(band)" title="Gojira (band)">Gojira</a> as supporting acts.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> On August 7, 2017, Metallica was invited by the <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Giants" title="San Francisco Giants">San Francisco Giants</a> again for the fifth annual "Metallica Night" with Hammett and Hetfield performing the national anthem.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> In January 2018, the band announced that they would be reissuing <i>The $5.98 E.P.: Garage Days Re-Revisited</i> on April 13 for <a href="/wiki/Record_Store_Day" title="Record Store Day">Record Store Day</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup> and the sixth annual "Metallica Night" was also announced a few weeks later, this time in April, with all proceeds going to the All Within My Hands Foundation, which the band created in late 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup> In February 2018, the band announced a second set of North American tour dates, most of which for cities that they had not visited in up to thirty years.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="S.26M2_and_upcoming_eleventh_studio_album_.282019.E2.80.93present.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="S&amp;M2_and_upcoming_eleventh_studio_album_(2019–present)"><i>S&amp;M2</i> and upcoming eleventh studio album (2019–present)</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Metallica_at_Ippodromo_San_Siro,_Milan,_May_8th,_2019.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Metallica_at_Ippodromo_San_Siro%2C_Milan%2C_May_8th%2C_2019.jpg/220px-Metallica_at_Ippodromo_San_Siro%2C_Milan%2C_May_8th%2C_2019.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Metallica_at_Ippodromo_San_Siro%2C_Milan%2C_May_8th%2C_2019.jpg/330px-Metallica_at_Ippodromo_San_Siro%2C_Milan%2C_May_8th%2C_2019.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Metallica_at_Ippodromo_San_Siro%2C_Milan%2C_May_8th%2C_2019.jpg/440px-Metallica_at_Ippodromo_San_Siro%2C_Milan%2C_May_8th%2C_2019.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3968" data-file-height="2976" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Metallica_at_Ippodromo_San_Siro,_Milan,_May_8th,_2019.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Metallica performing in Milan in 2019</div></div></div>
<p>In March 2019, Metallica announced that it would perform at the grand opening of San Francisco's new <a href="/wiki/Chase_Center" title="Chase Center">Chase Center</a> with the San Francisco Symphony in September to celebrate the twenty-year anniversary of <i>S&amp;M</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup> The commemorative shows, titled <i>S&amp;M2</i>, will feature arrangements from the original <i>S&amp;M</i> concerts as well as new arrangements for songs recorded since then, and will be directed by conductor <a href="/wiki/Michael_Tilson_Thomas" title="Michael Tilson Thomas">Michael Tilson Thomas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-UCR_169-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UCR-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BillboardS&amp;M2_170-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BillboardS&amp;M2-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup> In July, the band announced that the shows would be screened in over 3,000 theaters worldwide on October 9, with tickets going on sale in August.<sup id="cite_ref-UCR_169-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UCR-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BillboardS&amp;M2_170-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BillboardS&amp;M2-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In an interview with Australian magazine <i><a href="/wiki/The_Music_(magazine)" title="The Music (magazine)">The Music</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s official podcast in March 2019, Robert Trujillo said that Metallica had begun jamming on new material for its next studio album. "I'm excited about the next record because I believe it will also be a culmination of the two [previous] records and another journey. There's no shortage of original ideas, that's the beauty of being in this band." He estimated that the album would be released "a lot sooner than the previous two did... this time around I think we'll be able to jump on it a lot quicker and jump in the studio and start working. We've all vowed to get this one going sooner than later."<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> In an interview with Australian magazine <i>Mixdown</i> the following month, Kirk Hammett said that the band had tentative plans to enter the studio after its WorldWired Tour concluded in November. He stated, "We're in our third year since <i>Hardwired</i>. Maybe we can get a bit more focus and go into the studio a bit sooner." After not contributing any writing to <i>Hardwired... to Self-Destruct</i>, Hammett said regarding his ideas for the new album, "I have a ton of material. I've over-compensated, so I'm ready to go anytime."<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Style_and_lyrical_themes">Style and lyrical themes</span></h2>
<table role="presentation" class="mbox-small noprint" style="background-color:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;color:#000;">
<tbody><tr>
<td class="mbox-image"><div class="center"><div class="floatnone"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/50px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="50" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/75px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/100px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="160" data-file-height="160" /></div></div></td>
<td class="mbox-text plainlist" style="line-height:1.1em"><div class="haudio">
<div style="padding:4px 0"><a href="/wiki/File:Metallica_-_Damage_Inc.ogg" title="File:Metallica - Damage Inc.ogg">"Damage Inc." (1986)</a></div>

<div class="description" style="padding:2px 0 0 0">"Damage Inc." (<i>Master of Puppets</i>), demonstrating Metallica's fast tempo, and aggressive musicianship featured in early releases</div></div><hr /><div class="haudio">
<div style="padding:4px 0"><a href="/wiki/File:Metallica_-_Sad_But_True.ogg" title="File:Metallica - Sad But True.ogg">"Sad but True" (1991)</a></div>
<div><div class="mediaContainer" style="width:220px"><audio id="mwe_player_1" controls="" preload="none" style="width:220px" class="kskin" data-durationhint="30.000612244898" data-startoffset="0" data-mwtitle="Metallica_-_Sad_But_True.ogg" data-mwprovider="local"><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/0/0a/Metallica_-_Sad_But_True.ogg" type="audio/ogg; codecs=&quot;vorbis&quot;" data-title="Original Ogg file (60 kbps)" data-shorttitle="Ogg source" data-width="0" data-height="0" data-bandwidth="59826" /><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/transcoded/0/0a/Metallica_-_Sad_But_True.ogg/Metallica_-_Sad_But_True.ogg.mp3" type="audio/mpeg" data-title="MP3" data-shorttitle="MP3" data-transcodekey="mp3" data-width="0" data-height="0" data-bandwidth="171424" /></audio></div></div>
<div class="description" style="padding:2px 0 0 0">"Sad but True" (<i>Metallica</i>); Robert Palmer of <i>Rolling Stone</i> believed the band abandoned fast <a href="/wiki/Tempos" class="mw-redirect" title="Tempos">tempos</a> to expand its music and expressive <a href="/wiki/Range_(music)" title="Range (music)">range</a> in 1991</div></div><hr /><div class="haudio">
<div style="padding:4px 0"><a href="/wiki/File:Metallica_-_Purify.ogg" title="File:Metallica - Purify.ogg">"Purify" (2003)</a></div>

<div class="description" style="padding:2px 0 0 0">"Purify" (<i>St. Anger</i>), demonstrating Metallica's new musical approach with no guitar solos, a "raw, unpolished" sound, and Ulrich's <a href="/wiki/Snare_drum" title="Snare drum">snare drum</a></div></div></td></tr>
<tr><td colspan="2" class="mbox-text" style="line-height:1.1em"><hr /><i class="selfreference">Problems playing these files? See <a href="/wiki/Help:Media" title="Help:Media">media help</a>.</i></td></tr>
</tbody></table>
<p>Metallica was influenced by early heavy metal and hard rock bands and artists <a href="/wiki/Black_Sabbath" title="Black Sabbath">Black Sabbath</a>, <a href="/wiki/Deep_Purple" title="Deep Purple">Deep Purple</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kiss_(band)" title="Kiss (band)">Kiss</a>, <a href="/wiki/Led_Zeppelin" title="Led Zeppelin">Led Zeppelin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Queen_(band)" title="Queen (band)">Queen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ted_Nugent" title="Ted Nugent">Ted Nugent</a>, <a href="/wiki/AC/DC" title="AC/DC">AC/DC</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rush_(band)" title="Rush (band)">Rush</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aerosmith" title="Aerosmith">Aerosmith</a>, <a href="/wiki/Judas_Priest" title="Judas Priest">Judas Priest</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scorpions_(band)" title="Scorpions (band)">Scorpions</a><sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup> and by <a href="/wiki/New_wave_of_British_heavy_metal" title="New wave of British heavy metal">new wave of British heavy metal</a> (NWOBHM) bands <a href="/wiki/Venom_(band)" title="Venom (band)">Venom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mot%C3%B6rhead" title="Motörhead">Motörhead</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saxon_(band)" title="Saxon (band)">Saxon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Diamond_Head_(English_band)" title="Diamond Head (English band)">Diamond Head</a>, <a href="/wiki/Blitzkrieg_(band)" title="Blitzkrieg (band)">Blitzkrieg</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Iron_Maiden" title="Iron Maiden">Iron Maiden</a>, and early <a href="/wiki/Punk_rock" title="Punk rock">punk rock</a> bands <a href="/wiki/Ramones" title="Ramones">Ramones</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sex_Pistols" title="Sex Pistols">Sex Pistols</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Misfits_(band)" title="Misfits (band)">Misfits</a> also influenced Metallica's style as did <a href="/wiki/Post-punk" title="Post-punk">post-punk</a> band <a href="/wiki/Killing_Joke" title="Killing Joke">Killing Joke</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Rolling_Stone_174-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rolling_Stone-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup> The band's early releases contained fast tempos, harmonized leads, and nine-minute instrumental tracks. Steve Huey of AllMusic said <i>Ride the Lightning</i> featured "extended, progressive epics; tight, concise groove-rockers".<sup id="cite_ref-Ride_the_Lightning_-_Metallica_175-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ride_the_Lightning_-_Metallica-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup> Huey said Metallica expanded its compositional technique and range of expression to take on a more aggressive approach in following releases, and lyrics dealt with personal and socially conscious issues.<sup id="cite_ref-Ride_the_Lightning_-_Metallica_175-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ride_the_Lightning_-_Metallica-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup>  Religious and military leaders, rage, insanity, monsters, and drugs—among other themes—were explored on <i>Master of Puppets</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Master_of_Puppets_-_Metallica_176-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Master_of_Puppets_-_Metallica-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1991, Huey said Metallica with new producer Bob Rock simplified and streamlined its music for a more commercial approach to appeal to mainstream audiences.<sup id="cite_ref-Metallica_AMG_177-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Metallica_AMG-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Robert_Palmer_(writer)" title="Robert Palmer (writer)">Robert Palmer</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> said the band abandoned its aggressive, fast tempos to expand its music and expressive <a href="/wiki/Range_(music)" title="Range (music)">range</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Metallica_RS_review_178-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Metallica_RS_review-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup> The change in direction proved commercially successful; <i>Metallica</i> was the band's first album to peak at number one on the <i>Billboard</i> 200. Metallica noticed changes to the rock scene created by the <a href="/wiki/Grunge" title="Grunge">grunge</a> movement of the early 1990s. In <i>Load</i>—an album that has been described as having "an almost <a href="/wiki/Alternative_rock" title="Alternative rock">alternative rock</a>" approach—the band changed musical direction and focused on non-metal influences.<sup id="cite_ref-Metallica_-_ReLoad_179-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Metallica_-_ReLoad-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup> Metallica's new lyrical approach moved away from drugs and monsters, and focused on anger, loss, and retribution. Some fans and critics were not pleased with this change, which included haircuts, the cover art of <i>Load</i>, and headlining the <a href="/wiki/Lollapalooza" title="Lollapalooza">Lollapalooza</a> festival of 1996.<sup id="cite_ref-Load_review_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Load_review-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/David_Fricke" title="David Fricke">David Fricke</a> of <i>Rolling Stone</i> described the move as "goodbye to the moldy stricture and dead-end Puritanism of no-frills thrash", and called <i>Load</i> the heaviest record of 1996.<sup id="cite_ref-Load_review_54-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Load_review-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> With the release of <i>ReLoad</i> in 1997, the band displayed <a href="/wiki/Blues" title="Blues">blues</a> and early <a href="/wiki/Hard_rock" title="Hard rock">hard rock</a> influences, incorporating more rhythm and harmony in song structures.<sup id="cite_ref-Metallica_-_ReLoad_179-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Metallica_-_ReLoad-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><i>St. Anger</i> marked another large change in the band's sound. Guitar solos were excluded from the album, leaving a "raw and unpolished sound".<sup id="cite_ref-St_Anger_by_Metallica_70-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-St_Anger_by_Metallica-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> The band used <a href="/wiki/Drop_C_tuning" title="Drop C tuning">drop C tuning</a>; Ulrich's snare drum received particular criticism. <i>New York Magazine</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s Ethan Brown said it "reverberates with a thwong". The album's lyrics deal with Hetfield's drug rehabilitation and include references to the devil, anti-drug themes, claustrophobia, impending doom, and religious hypocrisy.<sup id="cite_ref-Music_Review_St._Anger_180-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Music_Review_St._Anger-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AMG_-_St._Anger_181-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AMG_-_St._Anger-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup> At the advice of producer Rick Rubin, for its ninth studio album <i>Death Magnetic</i>, the band returned to <a href="/wiki/Standard_tuning" title="Standard tuning">standard tuning</a> and guitar solos.<sup id="cite_ref-Metallica_Drummer_on_Producer_Rick_Rubin:_&#39;He&#39;s_Forced_Us_to_Rethink_Big-Picture_Stuff&#39;_182-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Metallica_Drummer_on_Producer_Rick_Rubin:_&#39;He&#39;s_Forced_Us_to_Rethink_Big-Picture_Stuff&#39;-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup> As a return to Metallica's thrash roots, <i>Death Magnetic</i> was a <a href="/wiki/Ostinato#riff" title="Ostinato">riff</a>-oriented album featuring intense guitar solos and subtle lyrics dealing with suicide and redemption.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legacy_and_influence">Legacy and influence</span></h2>
<p>Metallica has become one of the most influential heavy metal bands of all time, and is credited as one of the "big four" of thrash metal, along with Slayer, Anthrax, and Megadeth.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup> The band has sold more than 125 million records worldwide,<sup id="cite_ref-sold_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sold-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> including an RIAA-certified 66&#160;million and <a href="/wiki/Nielsen_SoundScan" title="Nielsen SoundScan">Nielsen SoundScan</a>-reported 58,000,000 in the US, making Metallica one of <a href="/wiki/List_of_best-selling_music_artists" title="List of best-selling music artists">the most commercially successful bands of all time</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup> The writers of <i>The Rolling Stone Encyclopedia of Rock &amp; Roll</i> said Metallica gave heavy metal "a much-needed charge".<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup> Stephen Thomas Erlewine and Greg Prato of Allmusic said Metallica "expanded the limits of thrash, using speed and volume not for their own sake, but to enhance their intricately structured compositions", and called the band "easily the best, most influential heavy metal band of the '80s, responsible for bringing the music back to Earth".<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Jonathan_Davis" title="Jonathan Davis">Jonathan Davis</a> of <a href="/wiki/Korn" title="Korn">Korn</a> said he respects Metallica as his favorite band; he said, "I love that they've done things their own way and they've persevered over the years and they're still relevant to this day. I think they're one of the greatest bands ever."<sup id="cite_ref-Why_they_Rule?_Metallica_189-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Why_they_Rule?_Metallica-189">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Godsmack" title="Godsmack">Godsmack</a> drummer <a href="/wiki/Shannon_Larkin" title="Shannon Larkin">Shannon Larkin</a> said Metallica has been the biggest influence on the band, stating, "they really changed my life when I was 16 years old—I'd never heard anything that heavy".<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup> Vocalist and guitarist <a href="/wiki/Robb_Flynn" title="Robb Flynn">Robb Flynn</a> of <a href="/wiki/Machine_Head_(band)" title="Machine Head (band)">Machine Head</a> said that when creating the band's 2007 album, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Blackening" title="The Blackening">The Blackening</a></i>, "What we mean is an album that has the power, influence and epic grandeur of that album <i>Master of Puppets</i>—and the staying power—a timeless record like that".<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Trivium_(band)" title="Trivium (band)">Trivium</a> guitarists <a href="/wiki/Corey_Beaulieu" title="Corey Beaulieu">Corey Beaulieu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Matt_Heafy" title="Matt Heafy">Matt Heafy</a> said that when they heard Metallica they wanted to start playing guitar.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/M._Shadows" title="M. Shadows">M. Shadows</a> of <a href="/wiki/Avenged_Sevenfold" title="Avenged Sevenfold">Avenged Sevenfold</a> said touring with Metallica was the band's career highlight, and said, "Selling tons of records and playing huge shows will never compare to meeting your idols <i>Metallica</i>".<sup id="cite_ref-Avenged_Sevenfold_Interview_194-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Avenged_Sevenfold_Interview-194">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/God_Forbid" title="God Forbid">God Forbid</a> guitarists Doc and Dallas Coyle were inspired by Metallica as they grew up, and the band's bassist John Outcalt admires Burton as a "rocker".<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ill_Ni%C3%B1o" title="Ill Niño">Ill Niño</a> drummer <a href="/wiki/Dave_Chavarri" title="Dave Chavarri">Dave Chavarri</a> said he finds early Metallica releases are "heavy, raw, rebellious. It said, 'fuck you'",<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Adema" title="Adema">Adema</a> drummer Kris Kohls said the band is influenced by Metallica.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On April 4, 2009, Metallica were inducted into the <a href="/wiki/Rock_And_Roll_Hall_Of_Fame" class="mw-redirect" title="Rock And Roll Hall Of Fame">Rock And Roll Hall Of Fame</a>. They entered the Rock and Roll Hall of Fame the second year they were eligible and first year they were nominated. Metallica's induction into the Hall included its current lineup, <a href="/wiki/James_Hetfield" title="James Hetfield">James Hetfield</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kirk_Hammett" title="Kirk Hammett">Kirk Hammett</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Trujillo" title="Robert Trujillo">Robert Trujillo</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Lars_Ulrich" title="Lars Ulrich">Lars Ulrich</a>, and former members <a href="/wiki/Jason_Newsted" title="Jason Newsted">Jason Newsted</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cliff_Burton" title="Cliff Burton">Cliff Burton</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/MTV" title="MTV">MTV</a> ranked Metallica the third "Greatest Heavy Metal Band in History".<sup id="cite_ref-Why_they_Rule?_Metallica_189-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Why_they_Rule?_Metallica-189">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup> Metallica was ranked 42nd on <a href="/wiki/VH1" title="VH1">VH1</a>'s "100 Greatest Artists Of All Time",<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup> was listed fifth on VH1's "100 Greatest Artists of Hard Rock",<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup> and the band was number one on VH1's "20 Greatest Metal Bands" list.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> placed the band 61st on its list of "The 100 Greatest Artists of All Time";<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup> its albums <i>Master of Puppets</i> and <i>Metallica</i> were ranked at numbers 167 and 252 respectively on the magazine's list of <i><a href="/wiki/The_500_Greatest_Albums_of_All_Time" class="mw-redirect" title="The 500 Greatest Albums of All Time">The 500 Greatest Albums of All Time</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup> <i>Master of Puppets</i> was named in <i>Q Magazine</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;s</span> "50 Heaviest Albums of All Time",<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup> and was ranked number one on IGN's "Top 25 Metal Albums",<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup> and number one on Metal-rules.com's "Top 100 Heavy Metal Albums" list.<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup> "<a href="/wiki/Enter_Sandman" title="Enter Sandman">Enter Sandman</a>" was ranked number 399 on <i>Rolling Stone</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;s</span> "500 Greatest Songs of All Time".<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><i><a href="/wiki/Kerrang" class="mw-redirect" title="Kerrang">Kerrang</a>!</i> released a tribute album titled <i>Master of Puppets: Remastered</i> with the April 8, 2006, edition of the magazine to celebrate the 20th anniversary of <i>Master of Puppets</i>. The album featured cover versions of Metallica songs by Machine Head, <a href="/wiki/Bullet_for_My_Valentine" title="Bullet for My Valentine">Bullet for My Valentine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chimaira" title="Chimaira">Chimaira</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mastodon_(band)" title="Mastodon (band)">Mastodon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mendeed" title="Mendeed">Mendeed</a>, and Trivium—all of which are influenced by Metallica. At least 15 Metallica tribute albums have been released. On September 10, 2006, Metallica guest starred on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Simpsons" title="The Simpsons">The Simpsons</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span> eighteenth-season premiere, "<a href="/wiki/The_Mook,_the_Chef,_the_Wife_and_Her_Homer" title="The Mook, the Chef, the Wife and Her Homer">The Mook, the Chef, the Wife and Her Homer</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup> Hammett's and Hetfield's voices were used in three episodes of the animated television series <i><a href="/wiki/Metalocalypse" title="Metalocalypse">Metalocalypse</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup> Finnish <a href="/wiki/Cello_metal" class="mw-redirect" title="Cello metal">cello metal</a> band Apocalyptica released a tribute album titled <i><a href="/wiki/Plays_Metallica_by_Four_Cellos" title="Plays Metallica by Four Cellos">Plays Metallica by Four Cellos</a></i>, which features eight Metallica songs played on cellos. A parody band named <a href="/wiki/Beatallica" title="Beatallica">Beatallica</a> plays music using a combination of <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles" title="The Beatles">The Beatles</a> and Metallica songs. Beatallica faced legal troubles when <a href="/wiki/Sony" title="Sony">Sony</a>, which owns The Beatles' catalog, issued a <a href="/wiki/Cease_and_desist" title="Cease and desist">cease and desist</a> order, claiming "substantial and irreparable injury" and ordering the group to pay damages. Ulrich, a fan of Beatallica, asked Metallica's lawyer Peter Paterno to help settle the case.<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On March 7, 1999, Metallica was inducted into the San Francisco Walk of Fame. The mayor of San Francisco, <a href="/wiki/Willie_Lewis_Brown,_Jr." class="mw-redirect" title="Willie Lewis Brown, Jr.">Willie Brown</a>, proclaimed the day "Official Metallica Day".<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup> The band was awarded the <a href="/wiki/MTV_Icon" title="MTV Icon">MTV Icon</a> award in 2003, and a concert paying tribute to the band with artists performing its songs was held. Performances included <a href="/wiki/Sum_41" title="Sum 41">Sum 41</a> and a medley of "For Whom the Bell Tolls", "Enter Sandman", and "Master of Puppets". <a href="/wiki/Staind" title="Staind">Staind</a> covered "Nothing Else Matters", <a href="/wiki/Avril_Lavigne" title="Avril Lavigne">Avril Lavigne</a> played "Fuel", hip-hop artist <a href="/wiki/Snoop_Dogg" title="Snoop Dogg">Snoop Dogg</a> performed "Sad but True", <a href="/wiki/Korn" title="Korn">Korn</a> played "<a href="/wiki/One_(Metallica_song)" title="One (Metallica song)">One</a>", and <a href="/wiki/Limp_Bizkit" title="Limp Bizkit">Limp Bizkit</a> performed "Welcome Home (Sanitarium)".<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <i><a href="/wiki/Guitar_Hero" title="Guitar Hero">Guitar Hero</a></i> video game series included several of Metallica's songs. "One" was used in <i><a href="/wiki/Guitar_Hero_III" class="mw-redirect" title="Guitar Hero III">Guitar Hero III</a></i>. The album <i>Death Magnetic</i> was later released as purchasable, downloadable content for the game. "Trapped Under Ice" was featured in the sequel, <i><a href="/wiki/Guitar_Hero_World_Tour" title="Guitar Hero World Tour">Guitar Hero World Tour</a></i>. In 2009, Metallica collaborated with the game's developers to make <i><a href="/wiki/Guitar_Hero:_Metallica" title="Guitar Hero: Metallica">Guitar Hero: Metallica</a></i>, which included a number of Metallica's songs. <a href="/wiki/Harmonix" title="Harmonix">Harmonix</a>' video game series <i><a href="/wiki/Rock_Band" title="Rock Band">Rock Band</a></i> included "Enter Sandman" and "Battery"; "Ride the Lightning", "Blackened", and "...And Justice for All" were released as downloadable tracks. In 2013, due to expiring content licenses, "Ride the Lightning", "Blackened", and "...And Justice for All" are no longer available for download.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards_and_nominations">Awards and nominations</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_awards_and_nominations_received_by_Metallica" title="List of awards and nominations received by Metallica">List of awards and nominations received by Metallica</a></div>
<p><b>Grammy Awards</b><sup id="cite_ref-Grammy_Award_winners&#160;–_Metallica_214-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Grammy_Award_winners_–_Metallica-214">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>1990: <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Metal_Performance" title="Grammy Award for Best Metal Performance">Best Metal Performance</a>&#160;– "<a href="/wiki/One_(Metallica_song)" title="One (Metallica song)">One</a>"</li>
<li>1991: <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Metal_Performance" title="Grammy Award for Best Metal Performance">Best Metal Performance</a>&#160;– "<a href="/wiki/Stone_Cold_Crazy" title="Stone Cold Crazy">Stone Cold Crazy</a>"</li>
<li>1992: <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Metal_Performance" title="Grammy Award for Best Metal Performance">Best Metal Performance</a>&#160;– <i><a href="/wiki/Metallica_(album)" title="Metallica (album)">Metallica</a></i></li>
<li>1999: <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Metal_Performance" title="Grammy Award for Best Metal Performance">Best Metal Performance</a>&#160;– "<a href="/wiki/Better_than_You_(Metallica_song)" title="Better than You (Metallica song)">Better than You</a>"</li>
<li>2000: <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Hard_Rock_Performance" title="Grammy Award for Best Hard Rock Performance">Best Hard Rock Performance</a>&#160;– "<a href="/wiki/Whiskey_in_the_Jar" title="Whiskey in the Jar">Whiskey in the Jar</a>"</li>
<li>2001: <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Rock_Instrumental_Performance" title="Grammy Award for Best Rock Instrumental Performance">Best Rock Instrumental Performance</a>&#160;– "<a href="/wiki/The_Call_of_Ktulu" class="mw-redirect" title="The Call of Ktulu">The Call of Ktulu</a>"</li>
<li>2004: <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Metal_Performance" title="Grammy Award for Best Metal Performance">Best Metal Performance</a>&#160;– "<a href="/wiki/St._Anger_(song)" title="St. Anger (song)">St. Anger</a>"</li>
<li>2009: <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Metal_Performance" title="Grammy Award for Best Metal Performance">Best Metal Performance</a>&#160;– "<a href="/wiki/My_Apocalypse" title="My Apocalypse">My Apocalypse</a>"</li>
<li>2009: <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Recording_Package" title="Grammy Award for Best Recording Package">Best Recording Package</a>&#160;– <i><a href="/wiki/Death_Magnetic" title="Death Magnetic">Death Magnetic</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-Grammy_Award_winners&#160;–_Death_Magnetic_215-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Grammy_Award_winners_–_Death_Magnetic-215">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>

</p>
